[{"id":43269,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/one-team-one-stat-cavs-defense-gets-even-worse","date":"2017-11-09","title":"One Team, One Stat -- Cleveland Cavaliers' defense goes from bad to worst","content":" It\u2019s not just that the Cleveland Cavaliers started the season 4-6. It\u2019s that they started the season 4-6 against what should have been one of their easier stretches of schedule. Six of their first 10 games were at home and seven were against teams that (before the season started) weren\u2019t expected to make the playoffs this season. Now, some of those teams \u2013 Indiana, New York and Orlando \u2013 look better than expected, but the Cavs have played a part in that with their disinterested defense and not-so-three-happy offense. Is this just a team on cruise control until the games count? Last season taught us that there\u2019s a big difference between the regular-season Cavs and the postseason Cavs . But at this point last year, Cleveland was 9-2 and on its way to a 23-5 record through Christmas. Cruise control came after the All-Star break. A string of wins would have the Cavs quickly climbing the Eastern Conference standings . They got Week 4 started right with a win over the Milwaukee Bucks on Tuesday. But a four-game road trip begins at 8 p.m. ET in Houston on Thursday, the first game TNT\u2019s double-header. Pace : 101.1 (15th) OffRtg : 108.9 (2nd) DefRtg : 112.4 (30th) NetRtg : -3.5 (24th) Team:  Per game stats | Advanced splits | Lineups | Game log Players:  Per game stats | On-off court | Player shooting History:  Season by season results | Advanced stats | Franchise leaders The Cavs have allowed 4.4 more points per 100 possessions than they did last season . That\u2019s the biggest increase in the league. THE CONTEXT  Through Wednesday\u2019s games, the league average is *down 2.1 points per 100 possessions from last season. So, relative to the league average, the Cavs are 6.5 points per 100 possessions worse defensively. On average (over the last 10 seasons), the difference between the best defense and the worst defense in the league is 12 points allowed per 100 possessions. So 6.5 is a big deal. * Typically, league-wide efficiency rises as the season go on. Right now, league-average points scored per 100 possessions is higher than it was at this point last season, which turned out to be the most efficient offensive season of the last 40 years. And that\u2019s a drop-off from a defense that wasn\u2019t very good in the first place. Cleveland ranked 22nd defensively last season , the lowest rank (on either end of the floor) for any LeBron James team in his 14 full seasons in the league and the lowest *defensive rank for any team that made The Finals in the last 40 years. * One team in the last 40 years ranked lower than 22nd offensively and made The Finals: The 1998-99 New York Knicks, who ranked 26th in offensive efficiency (and third defensively) in a lockout-shortened season. Of course, it\u2019s early. The Cavs are just 11 games into an 82-game schedule. Still, the earlier you start building good defensive habits, the better. Where they ranked defensively didn\u2019t matter to last year\u2019s Cavs through the first three rounds of the playoffs, but some of their worst habits were on display as they allowed the Warriors to score 118 points per 100 possessions in The Finals. Only one below-average defensive team \u2013 the 19th-ranked 2000-01 Lakers \u2013 has won The Finals in the last 40 years. Unless things change dramatically, this will be the third time the Cavs have been a below-average defensive team in the four seasons since James returned to Cleveland. The exception was 2015-16, when they ranked 10th defensively \u2026 and won the franchise\u2019s only championship. Just 11 games into the season, a team\u2019s improvement or drop-off could be partially a result of the schedule they\u2019ve played. The Cavs have played four games against the league\u2019s top 10 offenses , one more than the average team has. But that hasn\u2019t been the problem, as they\u2019ve had the league\u2019s worst defense against teams that don\u2019t rank in the top 10 offensively, allowing 110.6 points per 100 possessions in those seven games (while no other team has allowed more than 107.5 against the bottom 20). This early, a team\u2019s improvement or drop-off could also be a result of luck, and that\u2019s where there is some good news. The Cavs\u2019 defensive drop-off has come almost entirely as a result of their opponents\u2019 shooting. They\u2019ve actually improved in regard to defensive rebounding percentage and forcing turnovers (though they still rank in the bottom five in opponent turnover percentage ). They\u2019ve held relatively steady in regard to opponent free throw rate. The big difference has been opponent effective field-goal percentage . Shooting \u2013 how well you shoot and how well you defend your opponents\u2019 shots \u2013 is the most important thing in basketball. But on defense, you don\u2019t control shooting as much as you do on offense. Cavs opponents haven\u2019t shot much better in the paint or from mid-range than they did last season. The difference has been from beyond the arc, and given the value of the shots, a drop in 3-point defense is more damaging than a drop in interior defense. Corner threes have been a particular problem. Cavs\u2019 opponents have shot an incredible 43-for-80 (54 percent) from the corners. And the two corners have been equally damaging, as their opponents have shot 22-for-41 from the left corner and 21-for-39 from the right . The good news is that those percentages will come down, no matter what the Cavs do. Opponent 3-point percentage in a small sample size is noisy data. But it must be noted that the two teams that currently lead the league in opponent 3-point percentage are the same two teams \u2013 Golden State and Boston \u2013 that have ranked in the top five each of the last four seasons. How their opponents shoot from beyond the arc isn\u2019t totally out of the Cavs\u2019 control, as some of those looks from the corners have been too easy. On this possession from Tuesday, Giannis Antetokounmpo gets the ball on the block after a pick-and-roll, and all five Cleveland defenders are ball-watching, with three open shooters on the perimeter. Antetokounmpo finds Tony Snell for an open, in-rhythm shot in the right corner before James, who was in no-man\u2019s land (not helping, not staying at home on his man) can recover. TWO MORE CAVS NOTES  1. The Cavs have taken 35.1 percent of their shots from 3-point range, down from 39.9 percent last season. Four seasons ago , 35.1 percent would have been the highest rate in the league. Two seasons ago , the Cavs ranked third at 35.2 percent. This season, with the league continuing to shot more from beyond the arc, 35.1 percent ranks 12th and the drop from 39.9 percent ranks as the league\u2019s biggest reduction from last season, with 20 of the 30 teams seeing an increase in the percentage of their shots that have come from 3-point range. Only once in their last 283 games (including playoffs) have the Cavs attempted fewer threes than they did in Tuesday\u2019s win over Milwaukee , when they were 9-for-18 from beyond the arc. Even with that 50-percent performance, the Cavs have also had the third biggest drop in 3-point percentage (from 38.4 percent to 34.4 percent) from last season. Combine that with the drop in attempts and the Cavs are scoring almost nine fewer points per game from beyond the arc. Another drop of note: 24 percent of their threes have come from the corners, down from 31 percent last season, when they set an NBA record with 353 corner threes. LeBron James leads the league on assists on corner threes, but has assisted on 1.4 per game, down from 2.2 last season. The drop in corner rate contributes to the drop in 3-point percentage, because the Cavs (like most teams) shoot corner threes better than above-the-break threes. You can pin the change on some of the Cavs\u2019 new personnel. Over the past three seasons, Jeff Green, Derrick Rose and Dwyane Wade have shot a combined 29 percent on threes, which have accounted for just 17 percent of their field goal attempts. None of them fit the Cavs\u2019 formula for offensive success over the last three years, which was to surround James with as much shooting as possible. In each of the last two seasons, the Cavs had eight players who have shot 35 percent or better on at least 750 career 3-point attempts. This season, they only have *five. * They gained Jose Calderon, but lost Kyrie Irving, James Jones, Richard Jefferson and Deron Williams. Through 11 games, the Cavs have shot better and more often from 3-point range with none of the Green-Rose-Wade trio on the floor than they have with one. And they\u2019ve shot better and more often from 3-point range with only one of those three guys on the floor than they have with two or three. Even with the drops in 3-point attempts and percentage, the Cavs still rank as the league\u2019s No. 2 offense. They\u2019ve scored 2.0 fewer points per 100 possessions than they did last season, but that\u2019s a smaller drop than the league average (2.1). They\u2019ve made up for the drop in threes (and an increase in turnover percentage ) with more shots and better shooting in the restricted area. They\u2019re still below the league average in regard to the percentage of their shots that have come from the restricted area, but have seen a small increase from 30 to 31 percent. With James leading the way and with Kevin Love much improved (55 percent last season , 74 percent this season), the Cavs have shot a league-best 71.6 percent in the restricted area . A decrease in perimeter shooting should have an adverse effect on the ability of James to get into the paint and finish, but that hasn\u2019t been the case. He has taken 49 percent of his shots , the highest rate of his career, from the restricted area. In his 15th season, he\u2019s registering career-high marks in both effective field goal percentage and true shooting percentage. It\u2019s a different Cavs offense, and it will evolve as the season goes along. After a slow start, J.R. Smith has shot 8-for-13 from 3-point range over the last three games, Cleveland\u2019s best offensive stretch of the season so far. But it will be interesting to see how Isaiah Thomas affects the shot chart when he returns from his hip injury and if any of the Green-Rose-Wade trio are on the floor when Cleveland needs to score late in a big game. 2. The Cavs have been outscored by 12.2 points per 100 possessions in the first quarter. . So far this season, you\u2019ve been able to determine early on whether or not the Cavs are engaged. Often, they haven\u2019t been. They\u2019ve lost five first quarters by nine or more points, and only three times have they had a lead at the end of the first. The Cavs have been much better in the second quarter ( plus-6.7 per 100 possessions ), with equal improvement on both offense and defense. But while they\u2019ve made some pseudo comebacks, the only team against which they\u2019ve been able to climb out of hole and win a game is the 2-7 Chicago Bulls. When the Cavs have been tied or ahead at the end of the first quarter, they\u2019re 4-0. When they\u2019ve trailed at the end of the first quarter, they\u2019re 1-6 . The league also fined Westbrook, Paul George and coach Billy Donovan $15,000 apiece for their criticisms of the officials after the call against Anthony on Sunday. Both were unusual plays in that flagrant fouls are usually called against defensive players. Instead, Anthony and Westbrook were whistled for contact they created while attempting shots. Anthony drove to the basket and elbowed center Jusuf Nurkic in the face on a shot that went in during the Thunder\u2019s loss in Portland on Sunday. The basket was overturned after review and Anthony was hit with the automatic ejection. Crew chief Rodney Mott said after the game that referees ruled the contact was excessive and not a natural basketball move and the league agreed. \u201cWe reviewed it, the same as we review all plays of this nature, and agree with the on-court officials that the foul met the criteria of hard contact above the shoulders with high potential for injury,\u201d NBA spokesman Tim Frank said. \u201cWhile attempting to draw a foul, Anthony extended his elbow into his opponent\u2019s face, which is dangerous and reckless in nature.\u201d Westbrook was attempting a jump shot Tuesday against Sacramento when he and defender Bogdan Bogdanovic collided. Westbrook was issued a flagrant 1 foul, but that was downgraded. \u201cAfter review, we determined that the contact was part of Russell\u2019s downward shooting motion and the defender was moving forward into his shooting space,\u201d Frank said. A flagrant 1 is considered unnecessary contact. The flagrant 2 is deemed unnecessary and excessive \u2013 and a foul doesn\u2019t have to be considered intentional to be determined dangerous. The league reviews all flagrants and can upgrade, rescind or leave them as called on the floor. If a player exceeds five flagrant foul points during the season, he will be suspended for the next game."},{"id":48578,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/new-york-knicks-kristaps-porzingis-out-wednesday-game","date":"2017-11-08","title":"Kristaps Porzingis bothered by elbow injury, eyes future procedure","content":" New York star forward Kristaps Porzingis missed the Knicks\u2019 game Wednesday night against the Orlando Magic because of a sprained ankle and an elbow injury. The Associated Press contributed to this report."},{"id":43274,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/week-history-milwaukee-bucks-seattle-sonics-5-overtime-game-1989","date":"2017-11-08","title":"This Week In History: Milwaukee Bucks, Seattle Sonics stage 5OT classic","content":"When the Seattle Supersonics visited the Milwaukee Bucks on Nov. 9, 1989, who would have known the teams would engage in one of the longest games in NBA history. Six different players scored 20 or more points in the Bucks\u2019 155-154 victory that took five overtimes to complete. The game, at the time, was the longest in NBA history in the shot-clock era and wasn\u2019t sealed up until the Bucks\u2019 Tony Brown and Jeff Grayer got hot in the fifth overtime period. The duo helped score nine consecutive points in that frame that put Milwaukee up 155-146 with 34 seconds remaining. The Sonics put forth one last spurt of their own \u2014 an 8-0 run \u2014 but it fell short of forcing a sixth OT period. For the losing Sonics, Dale Ellis led the way with 53 points on 18-for-39 shooting (he was also 14-for-17 from the free throw line). His teammates Xavier McDaniel and Derrick McKey added 37 and 24 points, respectively. McDaniel had a chance to win the game at the buzzer, but his 3-pointer bounced off the back iron. For the Bucks, Ricky Pierce led the way with 36 points on 15-for-21 shooting, while Alvin Robertson (28 points) and Jack Sikma (23 points) chipped in as well. The longest game in league history was played on Jan. 6, 1951, when the Indianapolis Olympians beat the Rochester Royals, 75-73, in six overtimes. The long, lonely hours of rehab work on the right leg he shattered in Las Vegas while playing with Team USA . And, worse, the dread that his career might be over that weighed on him mentally even after most of the physical chores were done. \u201cIt\u2019s not the work. You\u2019re fine with the work,\u201d George said, back to his All-Star self, now with the Oklahoma City Thunder, after scoring 20 in a Halloween romp over the Bucks . \u201cWhat sucks is the repetitiveness. Continuing the same rehab, doing the same stuff for a whole year, that\u2019s where it bothers you. \u201cWhen you\u2019re playing, the game is different every night. But when you\u2019re rehabbing, when you\u2019re doing the same stuff over and over to build muscle, to build confidence, it sucks.\u201d Now, George was asked, imagine having to do it all again. Another lost year, the grind again, and all the uncertainty of what\u2019s next. \u201cThat would really suck.\u201d Jabari Parker knows all about it. He is living it, a Groundhog Day of a surgically repaired left anterior cruciate ligament. In the movie, Bill Murray at least mixed things up while stuck in the same place, messing with people, dialing up his risks, forcing some adventures. For Parker, about the only things that have changed are fresh scars that run parallel to his earlier set and the venue where he tackles his daily slogs. The first time, after blowing out his left knee in Phoenix in December 2015 , the Bucks made their practice home at a small college south of the city, close to Lake Michigan and equipped at a fairly basic level. Now, as the 6-foot-8 forward from Duke and product of Chicago\u2019s Simeon High grinds through the final months of that second ACL tear , he does so at a relative Taj Mahal of sweat and exertion. The Bucks\u2019 new practice facility is state of the art, offering nearly every apparatus and all the technology an athlete could need to ideally stay healthy but yes, to recover and rehab as well. But it\u2019s like cooking a familiar meal in a new high-tech kitchen \u2014 there are no shortcuts to the prep work, no hurrying through the baking time. ACLs need TLC, and a maddening level of monotony. \u201cThe only thing that\u2019s changed is really the environment,\u201d Parker said on Oct. 31. His teammates were in various stages of readying themselves to face the Thunder \u2014 glancing at the video breakdowns on the dressing room\u2019s big screen, taping and stretching and strapping while Parker tugged on the street sweats he\u2019d wear home. \u201cWork is work. It\u2019s the same equipment, actually,\u201d Parker said. \u201cIt\u2019s just better when you have a lot of bodies in the gym.\u201d Mostly Parker is around Suki Hobson, the team\u2019s strength and conditioning coach, and other members of the team\u2019s training and medical staffs. He brings a certain layman\u2019s expertise, too; remember, he spent 10 of the 26 months between his two knee blowouts doing virtually the same daily regimen. \u201cI don\u2019t find this very different,\u201d Parker said. \u201cJust things that I learned have been fundamental for me going forward. The only difference is that I know what I\u2019m going through. From there, second time\u2019s a charm.\u201d Parker, 22, has been healthy on his March 15 birthday just once in three NBA seasons and already has lost more games to injury than LeBron James has in 15 seasons . He occasionally will drop an aphorism into a conversation like a verbal crunch on which to lean: \u201cIf it doesn\u2019t kill me, it\u2019s just going to make me stronger.\u201d Or \u201cBad things happen for a good reason.\u201d But his true ability to cope comes from his devout Mormon faith, instilled by his mother Lola and exemplified by volunteer work Parker has done, the charities he supports and the social issues on which he\u2019s spoken. Only once since the second injury, he said, did he fall prey to the \u201cWhy me?\u201d question. That came and went fast, in the moments after he made a move to the basket against Miami Feb. 8 at the BMO Harris Bradley Center , felt the pop and the pain and knew what was wrong by the time he crumpled to the court. Otherwise, there\u2019s a calm about Parker, laced with optimism and even the serenity of flipping the keys to, and stress of, this to something greater. \u201cI\u2019m just a spiritual person, you know?\u201d he said, loud locker-room music pulsing beneath his words. \u201cI never forget what drives the vessel, what drives the ship. So if my spirit is good, anything is pretty much attainable. My dream is to come out of this, so I\u2019m just directing it accordingly.\u201d By the morning of Feb. 9 \u2014 if not sooner \u2014 Parker said he had steeled himself to the long rehab road ahead. \u201cI flipped a switch and said, \u2018Hey, you\u2019ve just got to get up. And work,\u2019 \u201d he said. \u201cMope? That\u2019s not going to do nothing for you, that\u2019s not going to do much for me. Just got to keep grinding. And never give up.\u201d At the time of the interview, Parker was said to be participating in about 70 percent of the Bucks\u2019 practice activities. He still was about three weeks from being cleared for real contact and 5-on-5, full-court scrimmaging, pushing that stage closer to Thanksgiving. He refuses to put a date on his return, lest he skip or rush through some steps, so Milwaukee is sticking to a vague February-ish timeline. After which, as Parker sees it, there still will be time to for 2017-18 to be productive. \u201cThis season is successful for me, personally, if I\u2019m able to play again,\u201d he said. \u201cGet better. Being efficient. Playing in the playoffs \u2014 I\u2019ve never done that, so that would be good to experience. And just make it through, take it day by day and game by game and see where it goes. \u201cThe basketball part comes naturally. There\u2019s only so much you can see from looking out, \u2018cuz I don\u2019t have, like, videos and they don\u2019t show me out there, right? It\u2019s just believing. That\u2019s the easy part. It\u2019s just trying to re-establish myself with the team again.\u201d Listening between the lines, there seems to be some strain or distance between Parker and the Bucks. Some of that\u2019s natural, given the questions that will linger over his ability to return a second time. Also, they couldn\u2019t negotiate the multimillion-dollar contract extension for which he and others in his 2014 first-round draft class were eligible this autumn. Parker grows terse, too, when asked if his coaches have given him any added duties to draw him close, the way Boston Celtics coach Brad Stevens has thrown video work at Gordon Hayward to keep him engaged through his ankle rehab. \u201cNext question,\u201d Parker said. Finding a valid comparison or role model for what Parker is trying to accomplish is difficult. Single ACL injuries are challenging enough in a sport built on jumping, running and applying extreme torque to lower extremities. One player who can relate, to a point, is Parker\u2019s fellow Simeon alum, Derrick Rose, who swears there was nothing in the drinking fountains of that school that led to their repeated injuries. \u201cYou have to be around the team. You have to do everything like you were playing,\u201d said Rose, the 2011 MVP who subsequently lost the equivalent of three seasons to knee, leg and other injuries. \u201cTravel with team, that type of stuff whenever you get the chance. You can\u2019t just stay home rehabbing, \u2018cuz you\u2019ll drive yourself crazy.  \u201cHaving faith and knowing that you can only control what you can control [helps]. Like, injuries happen. You can\u2019t sit there and moan or feel bad because of them, or you\u2019ll kill yourself on the inside. It\u2019s all about just getting over it the best way possible. Everybody\u2019s different. And having that family around so you have somebody to vent to, to talk to.\u201d Parker has leaned on his mother especially during this second rehab. And he visualizes not merely coming back but coming back better, which is what he did the last time. Averaging 20.1 points, 6.2. rebounds and 2.8 assists per game, Parker was stirring some All-Star reserve talk before he went down. He appeared to be in the best shape of his life, and he had stretched his shooting range to legitimate 3-point territory, making 36.5 percent on 178 attempts . In 101 previous NBA games, he had taken only 51 from deep. \u201cHe came back and he was killin\u2019,\u201d said Minnesota\u2019s Andrew Wiggins, who was drafted No. 1 to Parker\u2019s No. 2 three years ago. \u201cHe did real good. Some people say, when you get hurt, when you tear something, your leg is strong. He looked bouncy. He\u2019ll come back stronger. He\u2019s a hard worker.\u201d Said George, who contacted Parker after the February setback: \u201cHe was playing better than before. He was more athletic, more explosive. It was crazy. I think what sucks the most is, he\u2019s on the verge, he\u2019s right there in being a star in this league. He\u2019s in a great situation with a great organization. So, like, everybody\u2019s ready, everybody\u2019s waiting, for him to go over that hurdle. But he keeps getting bit by the injury bug.\u201d Instead, it\u2019s Parker having to wait for the Brinks truck \u2014 a five-year, $148 million extension \u2014 that backed up to Wiggins\u2019 account last month . George, Bucks coach Jason Kidd and Parker\u2019s teammate, Giannis Antetokounmpo (and the rest of the league), are waiting along with him. Parker sounds uniquely equipped to handle the unknowns in play, drawing on his first injury and return, relying on his faith and perhaps running Plan B through his head should the outcome this time be different. \u201cPeople look at this as a negative. They don\u2019t really look at it as a blessing,\u201d Parker said. \u201cBut what you do, you create your own story. Like, a lot of people walk around like they haven\u2019t been touched. And then when they face adversity, they don\u2019t know how to deal with it because it\u2019s the first time in their life. \u201cThere\u2019s basically nothing in my life that can make me quit, that can make me go under. It\u2019s the same with Derrick. Me and him just have a mental toughness where we\u2019ve dealt with everything before. So we just move forward. \u2026 We\u2019re able to show people that, if you dream big, those dreams can still stay alive if you stay positive. You can stay above water. \u201cReal people who have real issues will look at us. That\u2019s what makes me more humble.\u201d Steve Aschburner has written about the NBA since 1980. Through the first 158 games this season, teams were averaging 10.4 makes on 28.9 attempts \u2014 and that attempts number represents a 57 percent increase over what teams hoisted just six seasons ago (18.4). To me \u2014 and I suppose I\u2019m in the minority \u2013 this represents the death of the mid-range game, a significant loss in terms of creativity and individual expression on the court. Finger rolls, tear-drops, turnarounds, fadeaways, floaters, bank shots, sky hooks \u2014 those were part of the varied history of the NBA offensive game, offering a direct lineage to some of the league\u2019s greatest players. They gave kids signature moves to imitate in their driveways or at the playgrounds. Now we\u2019re working with a limited palette of layups, dunks and 3-pointers, and if young players are imitating anything, it\u2019s Steph Curry firing from 30 feet. Except there\u2019s precious little personality in anyone\u2019s 3-point attempt \u2014 if you\u2019ve seen one, you\u2019ve pretty much seen them all. This mournful rant already is too long, so I\u2019ll wrap by saying I look forward to the day the NBA moves the arc farther out, equalizes the risk\/reward factor and invites some old-school \u201ctwo\u2019s\u201d back into the game. I nominate his 14-for-16 effort against the Bucks as the day the earth stopped moving. Or maybe it was the backboard. I know it\u2019s early and the nearly 60 percent clip he\u2019s shooting from deep right now won\u2019t last. But for Gordon to show this kind of improvement on his outside stroke is a testament to his dedication to his craft, the one things NBA players rarely get credit for when they are in the often arduous process of transforming themselves from prospects to true players. Gordon\u2019s diligence should be applauded. Will this move help Milwaukee climb the Eastern Conference hierarchy and, if so, how?  * * * Steve Aschburner : Acquiring Bledsoe moves the Bucks into contention for one of the East\u2019s top four seeds, in my opinion. He\u2019s a potent, athletic scorer, a Top 50 talent in the league, and he\u2019s got something to prove after his clumsy (but ultimately effective) departure from Phoenix. Giannis Antetokounmpo and Khris Middleton need some help in Milwaukee\u2019s offense, more than just optimism about Jabari Parker\u2019s return. The backcourt depth presumably will make up for giving up helpful reserve Greg Monroe, and there will still be considerable minutes for last year\u2019s ROY Malcolm Brogdon. Shaun Powell :  Amazingly, this Bledsoe trade helps Giannis Antetokounmpo become a better player. Without the burden of having to run the offense \u2014 that\u2019ll be split by Bledsoe and Malcom Brogdon now \u2014 he can be turned loose to finish more plays and develop his catch-and-shoot skills, which is really the only area that can be classified as a mild weakness. Both Brogdon and Bledsoe can play off the ball and therefore Jason Kidd has multiple lineups and weapons to throw at the other bench. I\u2019m not ready to put Milwaukee in The NBA Finals yet, but if the Cavs don\u2019t get their act together (I suspect they will), the Bucks with Bledsoe (and a healthy Jabari Parker) will rattle the cage next spring. John Schuhmann : He probably can\u2019t hurt a team that\u2019s lost four straight and has slid to 29th in defensive efficiency . Bledsoe will give the Bucks some much-needed punch off the dribble, but more important is the other end of the floor, and the Bucks already have some good defenders in the backcourt. Regardless of personnel, Jason Kidd has to decide if he\u2019s going to stick with his aggressive defensive scheme that, despite the Bucks\u2019 collective length, more and more opponents are able to take advantage of for high rates of layups and corner threes. Sekou Smith : I think it will, in time, help the Bucks continue to climb the ladder in the Eastern Conference playoff chase. But if I\u2019ve learned anything during the early portion of this season, it\u2019s not to expect to see some immediate bump in the Bucks\u2019 fortunes. I\u2019m going to give this move some time. I\u2019m going to give Bledsoe some time to adjust to his new surroundings and I\u2019m certainly going to extend the same courtesy to his new teammates, who will have to rework their operation to account for a dynamic point guard like Bledsoe. Coach Jason Kidd\u2019s tutelage here will be crucial. But from a nuts and bolts standpoint, adding a 20-point, six-assist point guard with elite athleticism has to be a good thing \u2026 right? * * * * * *"},{"id":43279,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/jimmy-butler-working-get-andrew-wiggins-reach-full-potential","date":"2017-11-08","title":"Minnesota Timberwolves out to fuel Andrew Wiggins' rise to stardom","content":" * Tonight on ESPN:  Wolves at Warriors (10:30 ET) MINNEAPOLIS \u2014 It\u2019s not Andrew Wiggins\u2019 fault that he had the disadvantage of being drafted 29 spots higher than Jimmy Butler. Butler\u2019s story is the stuff of current NBA lore. Born and for a spell raised in the small Texas town of Tomball. Thrown out of the house at 13 by his single mother and sleeping on neighbors\u2019 and friends\u2019 sofas. Neglected by college recruiters, spinning a season at Tyler (Tex.) Community College into Buzz Williams\u2019 first scholarship at Marquette. Drafted with the last pick of the first round in 2011 , thrown scraps at the end of the Chicago Bulls\u2019 bench \u2026 Until he works and wills himself into a starter, the Kia Most Improved Player in 2015 , a five-year, $95 million contract , three All-Star appearances, one of the league\u2019s most complete two-way players and now the leader of a young and hungry Minnesota Timberwolves team. Wiggins is one of the cornerstone talents of that team, and his backstory hardly could be more different from Butler\u2019s. The son of elite athletes \u2014 his father, Mitchell Wiggins, played six seasons in the NBA and his mother, Marita Payne, was a Canadian Olympic sprinter \u2013 the Wolves\u2019 forward inherited a rare bundle of skills and capabilities. He was touted not just by his hometown but by an entire country, dubbed \u201cMaple Jordan\u201d as Canada\u2019s latest, greatest hoops hope. Butler spent a year in junior college just to earn a scholarship. Wiggins spent a year at NCAA powerhouse Kansas, eschewing his final three seasons to enter the NBA as the No. 1 overall pick in 2014 . He was coveted enough, without having played a minute in the league, to be traded for an All-Star when LeBron James made his surprise return to Cleveland that summer and tabbed Kevin Love to be part of a new Big Three with himself and Kyrie Irving. Thus, Wiggins joined a forlorn Minnesota organization 10 years into what has become a 13-year playoff drought. He cruised to the NBA\u2019s Kia Rookie of the Year award on a team that won just 16 games that season . The Wolves upped that to 29 and 31 victories the next two seasons, Wiggins boosting his scoring average to 20.7 points per game and 23.6 ppg while often failing to bust a gut or break a sweat. That, at least, was the reputation he developed, borne from his own admission in high school that he picked and chose the opponents and matchups against which he locked in. If only Wiggins played hard on both ends of the floor, they said. If only his motor revved high every night. If only he relied less on his talents and more on tenacity. If, if, if. Butler wants to change Wiggins\u2019 ifs to whens. And the way Butler is wired, when means now. \u201cMy job is to show him what it takes to win at both ends of the floor and how hard you have to play,\u201d Butler said over the weekend, four victories into what has grown to the five-game winning streak as Wolves face the defending-champion Golden State Warriors tonight. \u201cThe kid is so talented. Everything comes so easy for him. When he gets the mindset that, \u2018no matter how talented I am, I have to bring it on every single possession,\u2019 that\u2019s when you\u2019ve got to start talking how great can this kid be. That\u2019s what I want him to understand \u2013 you\u2019re one of the most talented players in the league. Don\u2019t take any possessions off.\u201d Butler is a plow horse who always lets you see him sweat, who got where he is today by dint of hard work. Wiggins is a thoroughbred to whom things seemingly have come easy, no straining necessary beyond the drills, workouts and games asked of any player. Neither characterization captures Butler or Wiggins in full, but both are close enough that the Wolves \u2014 and much of the NBA \u2014 are watching to see what how much of Butler rubs off on the younger man. \u201cI think I bring it every night,\u201d Wiggins said casually, not at all defensively, about the criticism he hears most frequently. \u201cThis year, we\u2019ve got a good team. So, if someone else is going, someone else is going. But I always bring my game.\u201d Actually, everything Wiggins has experienced or accrued so far has come from his potential. He was drafted for it, traded for it and most recently paid for it \u2014 a five-year, $148 million \u201cmax\u201d contract extension that starts in 2018. Team owner Glen Taylor took some grief for wanting to meet with Wiggins face-to-face before signing the deal, to make sure the budding star keeps growing his game. Now Taylor will notice Wiggins looking his way after hitting a tough shot or making a defensive stop, and smiling. Their contract is secure. Wiggins\u2019 on-court demeanor flows from his personality, a mostly quiet nature that can make him seem aloof. Close friends and teammates can draw him out when they catch him laughing, but that side rarely shows at Target Center or under the lights of the league\u2019s 28 other venues. \u201cWigs is just laid back off the court,\u201d said scorer Jamal Crawford, another veteran player and influence newly added by Minnesota coach and basketball boss Tom Thibodeau. \u201cHe\u2019s not one who craves attention. He just comes, does his job, goes home. He\u2019s really, really quiet in that regard. But he brings it \u2014 he has no problem making the big play or taking the big shot. He\u2019s not scared to fail, and that\u2019s a sign of an up-and-coming great player.\u201d Said Wiggins: \u201cThere are a lot of personalities on the court. Some people look like they\u2019re working hard but they\u2019re not. Some people who are working hard don\u2019t look like it.\u201d Butler trusts what he can see. As Minnesota\u2019s undisputed leader and updated version of Kevin Garnett as the Wolves\u2019 24\/7 jumper cables, he doesn\u2019t believe a player can modulate his performance against Golden State one night, Dallas the next, without getting bit. \u201cCan\u2019t have it,\u201d Butler said, the home dressing room otherwise empty after Saturday\u2019s victory over the Mavericks. \u201cEverybody in this league is an NBA player. That\u2019s where he has to grow. He\u2019s a terrific kid, human being, basketball player. But you\u2019ve got to have that killer instinct in this league. You\u2019ve got to have it, man. \u201cIt\u2019s not certain matchups, it\u2019s not against certain teams, it\u2019s not taking things personal. You take it to every team, every matchup. Where you match up to kill and to help this team at all costs.\u201d The more success the Wolves have, the more they crave. At 7-3, they\u2019re off to their best start through 10 games since 2001-02. Should they beat the Warriors, they would have the franchise\u2019s first six-game winning streak since late in the 2003-04 season \u2013 which also happens to be the last time Minnesota reached the playoffs. Wiggins, at 22, has shown signs of making every game an occasion to which he rises. During the winning streak, he has scored 20 points or more three times. Already, he ranks third on the Wolves\u2019 all-time list for scoring 20 or more with 143 such games, behind only Love (167) and Garnett (534). His game-winning, glass-assisted 3-pointer as time expired at OKC last month, sprung by Karl-Anthony Towns\u2019 dubious midcourt pick, might have been a fluke. But the work he put in against the Thunder five nights later was not; Wiggins startled his teammates and coaches by diving twice to the floor for loose balls, grunt work for a diva. Thibodeau and his staff preach and document \u201cfirst to the floor!\u201d but Wiggins only recently has become that guy. \u201cYou see Wigs diving on the floor, you\u2019re like, \u2018Oh man!\u2019 \u201d Crawford said. \u201cEverybody kicked it to another gear and it changed the complexion of that game.\u201d Against the Mavericks Saturday , Wiggins scored 23 points but worked diligently at guarding both Harrison Barnes (17 points) and Wesley Matthews (five) in a defensive tandem with Butler. Twenty-four hours later in blowing out Charlotte, he finished with 20 points on 8-of-12 shooting and nailed three consecutive jump shots in the third quarter. But he drew praise for hustling back on defense to thwart a 2-on-1 Hornets break, the Wolves already leading by 20. In Thibodeau\u2019s and Butler\u2019s world, Wiggins soon will match the former Bulls\u2019 defensive intensity, finally making good on the predictions when he was drafted in 2014 that he\u2019d be an instant defensive force. It has taken awhile, partly due to the culture of a losing operation, partly from what seemed intentional energy rationing by Wiggins. \u201cWhen he learns to use the angles and his athletic ability and his God-given length of his arms and his big hands,\u201d Butler said, \u201che\u2019s gonna be a helluva defender. Offense, he\u2019s got it all. Now we\u2019ve got to get him to think, \u2018I\u2019m gonna be as aggressive on defense as I am on offense.\u2019 That\u2019s when you\u2019re talkin.\u2019 \u201d Said Thibodeau: \u201cI see a progression. He\u2019s learned a lot from all his experiences. He worked incredibly hard all summer. He spent a lot of time here, in and out, and stayed focused on basketball. I think he\u2019s made a conscious effort to do more than just score. He\u2019s rebounding, he\u2019s playmaking, his defense has improved. And with the game on the line, he can make the play.\u201d Reflecting both Wiggins\u2019 development and Minnesota\u2019s makeover, the 6-foot-8 wing has a positive net rating for the first time in his career at 109.6\/108.3. He is averaging 19.9 points, 4.6 rebounds and 1.4 assists , though he sometimes still needs to have his switch flipped. \u201cHe still hasn\u2019t even scratched the surface,\u201d forward Taj Gibson said. \u201cHe can turn it on when he wants to turn it on. The [Oct. 30] game in Miami, I remember Jimmy telling him to just dunk the ball. And the very next play, he dunked it. And the play after that, he almost got poster-of-the-year for how high he jumped. He missed it on his own, that\u2019s how crazy it was.\u201d Wiggins is said to spend much of his free time playing video games or hanging with his dog Cassie . He doesn\u2019t pull back much of the curtain in interviews, perhaps as a way of tamping down requests. He\u2019s cordial, business-like and maddening to the Wolves media types who sift through his responses in search of sizzle. He defends the intensity of his defense since arriving in Minnesota, but without bristling. Questions about his tendency to fill the points column on score sheets, while sticking small numbers in the other columns, get deflected easily. Wiggins concurs when it\u2019s pointed out that Thibodeau is the first coach he\u2019s had for consecutive seasons since back in high school, but he offers only a shrug of a comment about it. \u201cMy first year here, I kind of established in my mind where I would fit on the court,\u201d Wiggins said. \u201cThe best areas for me on the court and recognizing how to get in those positions. Now I\u2019m just here.\u201d \u201cSometimes Andrew is misjudged,\u201d Thibodeau said. \u201cHe\u2019s a quiet sort of guy, but he\u2019s a very confident guy. It\u2019s easy to look at Jimmy and say \u2018He\u2019s this, this and this.\u2019 But you tend to forget where Jimmy was his first and second years, his third year, his fourth year. I think you can look at a lot of players in the league \u2013 a guy like Kawhi [Leonard], same thing. Every year they got a lot better but there were steps they had to take. And if you look at Andrew, every year he\u2019s made a big step. And he\u2019s still just 22 years old.\u201d Wiggins has been compared to some of the NBA\u2019s brightest lights, at least as far as his potential. Tracy McGrady is frequently mentioned. One Wolves team member, a little embarrassed, suggested Julius Erving. Crawford has been grasping for the perfect answer. \u201cWho does he play like? I\u2019ve been trying to figure it out, but I haven\u2019t thought of one yet,\u201d Crawford said. \u201cBut he\u2019s definitely one of those guys \u2013 I would go back to an early 2000\u2019s, late \u201890s type of guy. I\u2019m not sayin\u2019 McGrady but those type of guys, where the game comes really easy to \u2018em. I\u2019m thinking of a wing who can really create and make plays, and the game was so easy for him, and he did things so effortlessly.\u201d Doing difficult things effortlessly and making it appear so are two different things. That\u2019s why the education of Andrew Wiggins continues, with Butler committed to barking until his prot\u00e9g\u00e9 turns in reliably strong performances as a muzzle. \u201cYou tell him over and over and over again,\u201d Butler said, \u201cuntil he gets tired of hearing it coming out of your damn mouth and he buys into it and he does it. That\u2019s what I\u2019m doing. We\u2019re always smiling and joking around on the floor, because we love playing with one another. But at the end of the day, I think it\u2019s my job to make sure everybody shows up, every single night. \u201cYou hope he see where it takes this team, and how his level of play is going to [raise] everybody\u2019s level of play, and how it\u2019s contagious. The views on this page do not necessarily reflect the views of the NBA, its clubs or Turner Broadcasting."},{"id":43280,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/brad-stevens-reaches-back-his-college-days-help-boston-celtics-overcome-loss","date":"2017-11-08","title":"Early season adversity is putting spotlight on Brad Stevens' magical touch","content":" *Tonight on ESPN:  Lakers vs. Celtics (8 ET) When Brad Stevens lost Gordon Hayward, he rounded up the remaining group and delivered a simple yet direct message designed to keep them moving, tough as it was to do. \u201cI don\u2019t need you to do more,\u201d Stevens said. \u201cI need you to do better.\u201d It was well received by Kyrie Irving and Jaylen Brown, and also rookie Jayson Tatum and Al Horford, because the Celtics are surprisingly sitting at the summit in the Eastern Conference without their All-Star forward , who could miss most if not all of the season. But it also registered with Shawn Vanzant and Matt Howard, Shelvin Mack and Ronald Nored. Because, you see, Stevens actually lost Hayward twice, most recently to a gruesome ankle fracture. The first time was when Hayward left Stevens and Butler for the NBA after his sophomore year. Both times, the coach connected with a shortchanged lineup and forged a belief in his players that the goal and philosophy remained unchanged. The Butler Bulldogs regrouped without Hayward and returned to the NCAA championship game, a feat that, on the shock meter, supplanted the previous year when the mid-major Cinderella school nearly sucker-punched Duke at the buzzer. The Celtics, at least here in the early season, are on track to duplicate that. It says plenty about Stevens and his unflappable nature and attention to detail. Perhaps he is the right coach, then, in this situation with the Celtics, given his experience with such things. Actually, you can go a step further: When Stevens took Butler to the title game the first time, he became a wanted man in college basketball; all the big schools with a coaching vacancy (and some without one) made their pitch. But when he returned to the title game without Hayward the next year, this time his wanted poster circulated around the NBA. That repeat run effectively was the swinging mallet that shattered the notion in NBA circles that college coaches couldn\u2019t make the jump, a belief that held a measure of legitimacy, given those who tried and failed badly. At least in this particular case, Celtics boss Danny Ainge followed his instincts and especially his eyes. How could a coach motivate a team, without its star, back to the title game the very next year? What else was there to see? Stevens is coaching the Celtics right now because of the way Stevens coached Butler in 2010-11. That was enough to dismiss major concerns about his age (he was 36 when hired by Boston two years later) and his unfamiliarity with the NBA culture and his nearly zero experience in coaching NBA-level players and their egos. That season without Hayward is arguably on the Mount Rushmore of college coaching performances. That season, he had Mack, who became a career NBA backup point guard; Howard, a career overseas player; and a bunch of future 9-to-5ers. That\u2019s it. That\u2019s who lined up against mighty Connecticut while a disbelieving basketball nation looked on.  \u201cIt was a goal, to get back to the championship game, and everybody thought we were crazy to think like that because we lost Gordon,\u201d said Shawn Vanzant, a senior guard on that team. \u201cWell, we knew we could.\u201d Butler had seasoned returnees from the 2009-2010 team but no All-American candidates, nothing like that. If anything, it was a surprise the Bulldogs still had Stevens, who was understandably the hot coaching prospect in the country that summer. But by turning down all offers he showed a level of loyalty rarely seen among mid-major coaches who haven\u2019t yet cashed a big paycheck. That next season Butler hit a speedbump, though, bottoming out during a frigid winter stretch where they lost four out of five, including three in a row to the likes of Wright State and UW-Milwaukee. A conference loss at Youngstown on Feb. 3 put their chances of making the NCAA tournament in question and lowered their record to 14-9. How could they return as giant slayers when they were struggling in the Horizon League? \u201cWhen that happened, it wasn\u2019t one of those rah-rah kind of things with him,\u201d said Micah Shrewsberry, a former Butler assistant who\u2019s now on Stevens\u2019 staff with the Celtics. \u201cThat\u2019s what Brad is really good at, staying level headed. \u201cThe message was to move on to the next game, just refocus as a group. He said we\u2019re playing too tense, not playing relaxed. We had pressure because of what happened to us the year before and he took that pressure off of us. We needed to live more day by day, minute by minute, possession by possession and he refocused us back to that. He told the players that it was all about each possession, that\u2019s all you need to worry about.\u201d Well, Butler didn\u2019t lose again until the title game to UConn two months later. \u201cI guess,\u201d said center Emerson Kampen, \u201cwe got the message that things had to change and they had to change quickly.\u201d Unlike this year\u2019s Celtics, who have Irving as a certified NBA lead singer, Butler lost its leading scorer and designated bail-out player with Hayward and there was nobody with those credentials in the lineup to take his place. That\u2019s with all due respect to Mack and Howard, both fine players. Stevens had his team thinking what it could do collectively to compensate and the players brought into the idea. \u201cHe got everybody understanding his value to the team, his role and that if we concentrated our abilities together we can still do it, we can still get done what we need to get done,\u201d said Kampen, now a Butler assistant coach. \u201cHe\u2019s an unbelievable communicator. I was a walk-on, and you feel your role is super important whether that\u2019s the best player or somebody who doesn\u2019t get into the game.\u201d Butler won three of its first four tournament games by a combined six points, breaking brackets everywhere and making folks believe in Stevens, in case some were still skeptical about the coach. \u201cHe never panicked and so we never panicked either,\u201d said Vanzant. \u201cNo matter if it was a big school and we were underdogs, he gave us confidence. It was, \u2018Go out and do what we\u2019ve been doing all year and it\u2019s going to be fun.\u2019 A lot of our players didn\u2019t care who we played and where we played the game.\u201d The in-game adjustments that have impressed Irving (who called Stevens \u201can intellectual\u201d) were polished during the second tournament run when Butler needed the right play at the right time. Matthew Graves was the associate head coach that year and said Stevens was masterful with the dry erase board. \u201cHe does such a great job of preparation,\u201d said Graves, now the head coach at South Alabama. \u201cOnce we got into the tourney we were prepared and also got some breaks along the way and before you know it we\u2019re in the championship game. He\u2019s so good at picking out the exact points where you need to exploit defensively or what you can do offensively to help put your team in the best frame of mind. He allows the players to play free and think clearly and that showed in the pressure moments.\u201d When Stevens lost Hayward the second time, and once everyone\u2019s jaws and hearts were picked up off the floor after that horrific injury, once again he didn\u2019t panic. He told Tatum, the Celtics\u2019 highly regarded rookie, to become an opportunist and maximize the extra minutes. He wanted more defensive doggedness from Brown, who agreed with the coach. And the blueprint from the preseason was hastily rewritten. \u201cWe had to tweak a little what we\u2019ve had to do offensively,\u201d said Stevens. \u201cDefensively we tried to stay with what we what we started from day one. We just wanted everyone to do what you do best.\u201d Did everyone need to do more without Hayward? \u201cWhen somebody goes out, the thought is they have to do more,\u201d said Stevens. \u201cActually, they just have to do their job better.\u201d The Celtics have done that and take a nine-game winning streak into the Garden on Wednesday against the Lakers. Shrewsberry said the players have bought into those ideas, saying: \u201cGordon is still a big part of it obviously but we can still do the things we want to do. Brad\u2019s influence is calming and I think that settled the guys down.\u201d Brown said: \u201cThere was two ways to go. We could sulk until the season\u2019s over, or we could step up and play some basketball.\u201d Stevens is keeping Hayward in the loop by inviting him into strategy meetings and going over assignments, and says this is part of the rehab process. It\u2019s an idea he got from Orlando coach Frank Vogel, who dealt with Paul George\u2019s broken leg two years ago with the Pacers. Vogel and Stevens became friends when both coached in Indianapolis, so Stevens reached out. \u201cIt wasn\u2019t just about what Paul could help Gordon with, (given) what he was going through with the injury, but also how we could best brainstorm to keep him as engaged as possible,\u201d said Stevens. \u201cEngagement is really important. There is a physical aspect to recovery but there\u2019s also an emotional aspect to recovery and being a part of a team. You don\u2019t want to come back and not been engaged with everyone.\u201d Until the All-Star forward fully recovers, Stevens wants to keep the bond tight between Hayward, himself and the Celtics, and this is another well-timed strategy by the coach. This happens when you\u2019ve lost your basketball soulmate twice. You tend to get a bit protective. It was, after all, Bledsoe\u2019s social media mic-drop \u2014 the \u201cI Don\u2019t wanna be here\u201d tweet as the Suns got off to their 0-3 start \u2014 that ultimately set this trade in motion. Phoenix almost immediately distanced itself from the 6-foot-1 guard \u2014 GM Ryan McDonough didn\u2019t buy Bledsoe\u2019s claim that he meant not the Suns but a hair salon he allegedly patronized \u2014 and went 4-4 without him until agreeing to the deal with the Bucks, reported by multiple outlets Tuesday morning. The winner of this deal? Bledsoe, obviously. He was in limbo and about to begin lonely, less-than-optimal solo workouts at the Suns\u2019 practice facility while awaiting a ticket out of Phoenix. He got that, at a cost of fewer than 140 characters and a $10,000 fine from the NBA, and will be joining a team with legitimate ambitions to contend in the Eastern Conference. The Bucks are runner-up winners because Bledsoe, 28, is an athletic point guard who brings scoring and playmaking skills. He can lessen some of the workload for All-Star forward Giannis Antetokounmpo and shooter Khris Middleton, while relieving some pressure at the point position on Malcolm Brogdon, the reigning Kia Rookie of the Year. Bledsoe, expected to meet the Bucks Wednesday in San Antonio, can slide nicely into a lineup and rotation without much disruption, with Brogdon and Matthew Dellavedova still around for significant minutes and Jabari Parker working his way back from another knee surgery (he\u2019s slated to return in February). Bledsoe is under contract for this season and next for a total of $29.5 million. In his three appearances for the Suns last month, Bledsoe averaged 15.7 points, 2.3 rebounds and three assists, while shooting 40 percent. But in 66 games last season, those numbers were 21.1 ppg, 4.8 rpg and 6.3 apg in 33.0 minutes. Milwaukee \u2014 which gave up big man Greg Monroe and protected first- and second-round picks, according to reports \u2014 becomes Bledsoe\u2019s third NBA team after he spent three seasons with the LA Clippers and the past four with the Suns. Many hailed the deal as a deft move for the Bucks: Phoenix, for its part, rids itself of a disgruntled player to complete a sudden, early-season makeover that included coach Earl Watson\u2019s firing and assistant Jay Triano moving up as interim coach. The picks, whether they convey in 2018, 2019 or beyond, will further the Suns\u2019 long-term development with added youth. And Monroe, despite limited use this season, has per-36 minute averages of 15.5 points and 11.4 rebounds. For Monroe, the deal is an unfortunate end to his time in Milwaukee. When he signed with the Bucks in the summer of 2015 , Monroe was considered the most notable free agent to choose that small-revenue franchise. After an inconsistent initial season in his relocation from Detroit, \u201cMoose\u201d became a reliable reserve at both ends and finished sixth in balloting for 2017 Kia Sixth Man of the Year. But he also served as an indicator of just how rapidly the league has changed, too, when he picked up his $17.8 million option for this season rather than take his chances in the open market. A below-the-rim banger, Monroe can score in his matchups against opponents\u2019 Clydesdale reserves, but does not thrive in today\u2019s breezier, 3-point-focused style of play. Given Antetokounmpo\u2019s romps to the rim, the last thing the Bucks want is someone clogging up the lane. Bledsoe and the newfound depth of the Bucks\u2019 backcourt and wing positions should help Milwaukee play at the current fashionable pace, while creating the necessary amount of space. Thanks to a groundbreaking partnership between Turner Sports and Intel, NBA fans will be able to watch TNT\u2019s marquee matchups like never before, beginning with the 2018 NBA All-Star Game. The multiyear partnership makes Intel the exclusive provider of virtual reality for the NBA on TNT, using Intel True VR cameras to capture live game footage from multiple angles in order to allow fans to view the game from different locations throughout the arena.  Many fans would never be able to experience sitting courtside at an NBA game. But with this new technology, everyday fans can experience the game like the celebrities sitting courtside with their feet in the hardwood. Fans can choose to view the game from high in the stands to get a bird\u2019s eye view of the action or take the viewpoint of the photographers sitting on the baseline with the players coming right at them. In addition to allowing fans to choose their own viewing experience, Intel will be able to use its freeD technology to integrate 360-degree volumetric video into the VR experience. This will let fans freeze a moment of game action and view it from the player\u2019s point of view as if they were on the court. When something like that happens, I expect you to let the guys know about it.\u2019 And he said, \u2018I\u2019m on it.\u2019 \u201d It was one minute of one day of one week of the Los Angeles Lakers\u2019 road back to re-joining the NBA elite. It is not a road almost never traveled quickly, or without detours, divots and disappointments. It will not happen this season in Los Angeles, if it happens at all. But as Kobe Bryant finally fades into the franchise\u2019s lore, the Lakers have legitimate hope for a breakthrough sooner rather than later. They have set themselves up for the summer of 2018, as all of NBA world knows by now, to be significant free-agent players. But the present is worth contemplating, too. There is a lot more than Lonzo Ball \u2014 or Lavar Ball, for that matter \u2014 going on at Staples Center. The next year isn\u2019t going to be spent tanking. Not when Kyle Kuzma does things that the Lakers had no idea he\u2019d be able to do as a rookie. Or when Ingram starts to make those KD comparisons look less like pipe dreams. Or when Ball greets his dad\u2019s latest proclamation with a shrug. Or when Julius Randle brings the ruckus off the bench. Vets like Brook Lopez and Kentavious Caldwell-Pope are on-court stabilizers who have provided the spine of a halfcourt offense and respectable defense, and Corey Brewer, who came to town last season as part of the Lou Williams trade , is heralded by many for quiet leadership. But If the kids don\u2019t show that they\u2019re worthy of the league\u2019s best coming to town in free agency, none of the pomp and circumstance that team president Magic Johnson or GM Rob Pelinka dream up over the next nine months is going to matter. \u201cThe thing we talk about is our mentality,\u201d Pelinka said last week. \u201cThe way that Magic and Kobe brought it every night, those guys guide us in terms of the mentality, the way we want to play in every game \u2014 compete hard and play the right way. That\u2019s probably the word that\u2019s guiding us right now.\u201d After barely hanging on to beat the Memphis Grizzlies at Staples Sunday night \u2014 the Lakers blew a 22-point third-quarter lead \u2014 L.A. is .500. In the big picture, no great shakes, to be sure. But for a team that\u2019s won 27, 21, 17 and 26 games the last four seasons , 5-5 is significant progress. \u201cSome of the players have gotten older,\u201d Walton said. \u201cI think KCP coming over, just a hard-nosed player. He\u2019s been in that Eastern Conference, hard worker. He kind of helps set that tone. Brook\u2019s been a solid vet in this league for a long time. I think as BI grows as a player, he\u2019s a competitor. You watched him in college and he was the same way. It\u2019s just a group of guys that are bonding together and trying to figure this out together.\u201d Ball has the steepest curve \u2014 rookie point guard, for a boss who redefined the franchise and won five rings and is generally considered one of the top two or three ever to play the position. And who was as outgoing and boisterous as Ball is withdrawn in public. It doesn\u2019t matter if Ball talks a lot to the media. John Stockton and Oscar Robertson didn\u2019t have a lot to say while they were players, and they turned out to be fairly decent floor generals. What matters is if the 20-year-old Ball can inspire grown men who are playing for money \u2014 can tell them what to do, where to go, when they\u2019ll shoot and a hundred other things that a point guard must do nightly. The point guard isn\u2019t always popular, but he has to have the respect of the locker room. He has to lead. \u201cThat\u2019s what I\u2019m still working on,\u201d Ball said last week. \u201cUCLA helped me a little bit, with Coach (Steve) Alford being there, he helped me a lot with it. But I\u2019m still working on that. Because playing with grown men, you can\u2019t always be quiet. You have to get into them sometimes, especially in the locker room.\u201d Amidst the insanity that is Ball\u2019s daily life \u2014 the Facebook show and the Big Baller Brand and, well, dad \u2014 his numbers so far ( 8.8 points, 6.6 rebounds and 6.7 assists per game ) are fine for a rookie. His shot needs work, to be sure. But Ball never is off message or off balance. He answers questions quickly, but politely, with a kind of bemused detachment. \u201cA lot of the credit goes to him, honestly,\u201d Walton said. \u201cI don\u2019t know if his upbringing has prepared him for it, the insanity that comes with everyone always watching and judging everything that comes with being a star. But he just has this ability where it seems that it doesn\u2019t really get to him. He\u2019s calm. He doesn\u2019t seem like stress and pressure really affect him that much. \u201cHe\u2019s been a great teammate; the guys on the team love. It\u2019s impressive at 19 \u2014 well, he\u2019s 20 now \u2014 that he\u2019s able to handle the limelight like he is. I mean, he\u2019s on SportsCenter every single night. No matter what\u2019s happening, he\u2019s on there. Obviously a lot of people have a lot of different opinions, but he was raised properly. He handles himself, he handles situations, he handles his teammates with dignity and class.\u201d Ball does get ticked off, just not on the court. There are people that push his buttons. \u201cMy little brother for sure,\u201d Ball said. \u201cThe youngest one. They take pride in it.\u201d But on the court, Ball continues to never reveal himself. \u201cI was just taught, the team goes how the point guard goes,\u201d he said. \u201cIf I\u2019m mad or showing my frustration, the whole team\u2019s gonna be like that, techs, and people are going to go down. So I just try to keep the even keel. That\u2019s why I don\u2019t get too high or too low. I\u2019ve been playing like that my whole life. It\u2019s just natural for me.\u201d But there\u2019s low-key, and there\u2019s asleep. Ball barely looked at the basket during Thursday\u2019s loss in Portland, shooting just twice in 28 minutes and going scoreless in a three-point loss . It\u2019s part of the maturation process of a rookie point guard, but Ball has to at least be a threat on the court or teams will continue playing his passing lanes. Much is made of Ball\u2019s release on his jumper, but really, the Lakers are more concerned about his footwork than his shooting form. \u201cIt\u2019s like he\u2019s shooting a different shot every time,\u201d one Angeleno says. (Dennis Scott, our Turner Sports colleague who knows a thing or two about jumpers, says that as long as Ball\u2019s hands get square at the release point, where Ball starts his shooting motion doesn\u2019t matter that much.) But Ball has been working with assistant coaches Miles Simon and Brian Shaw to further diversify his offensive bag, shooting runners and floaters after practices and before games. Getting that shot down will be a key next step in his development and the Lakers expect he\u2019ll ultimately make enough 3-pointers to be credible. Ingram has shown that kind of jump in his second season. He was uncertain and disappeared for large chunks in 2016-17, when he shot just 36 percent for the first three-quarters of the season and was a nightly blow-by candidate on defense. But he got going in his last 21 games, all starts, after the All-Star break, when he raised his scoring average from eight points per game to 13.2, and his field goal percentage to 47.5 percent . He\u2019s carried that end over to this season\u2019s beginning, but he\u2019s also stronger (about 10 pounds) and is able to finish through contact. His handle is much improved, and he\u2019s now using his length to get to the rim in one or two long strides \u2014 much like Durant when the light when on for him in Oklahoma City around 2010 or so. Ten games into this season, he\u2019s averaging 14.8 ppg , including a game-tying putback in the final seconds of regulation against Washington that led to an overtime win. And, along with Larry Nance, Jr. (now out six weeks after breaking a bone in his left hand against Portland) and Lopez, Ingram was voted by the players as one of the team\u2019s captains. \u201cI think (it was) a little bit being into myself last year, not realizing how good I was until the last two months of that season,\u201d Ingram said. \u201cNow I\u2019m just trying to get back and relax, relax a little bit and trying to use my skill level and my ability. When I play my hardest, I feel like I\u2019m one of the best on the floor.\u201d Yet the revelation so far has been Kuzma, who came in the D\u2019Angelo Russell trade on Draft night . At the time, the supposed \u201cprize\u201d the Lakers got in the deal was moving Timofey Mozgov\u2019s remaining three years and $47.8 million from their books. Doing so would give them an unencumbered shot at a max free agent next summer and an outside shot at two if they could move another contract by next summer. But Kuzma has been a revelation. He never took more than 2.9 threes per game in three seasons at Utah , but he\u2019s taking four a night for the Lakers. He puts the ball on the deck like a 10-year vet who expects every shot to go in. He runs the floor and finishes. He talks on defense. He\u2019s averaging 15.4 ppg and shooting 56 percent from the floor \u2014 only Ben Simmons and Lauri Markkanen are scoring more per game among rookies . In his first start, for the injured Nance, Kuzma dropped 21 and 13 on the Nets , reminding them of the player they had for a few minutes. The Lakers had him on their short list before the Draft, along with Michigan\u2019s D.J. Wilson and Syracuse\u2019s Tyler Lydon. They thought each could be good in time, maybe a rotation player in a year or two. No one had this. Kuzma was a first-team all Pac 12 selection and a very good defensive player for Utah, but Oregon\u2019s Jordan Bell got the conference\u2019s Defensive Player of the Year award, and all the attention when the Ducks made the Final Four. Hitting on someone like Kuzma accelerates the calculus of a rebuilding team. You expect to get a star \u2014 a superstar \u2014 with the second pick. You do not expect that with the 27th pick, even if it\u2019s traded to you. That gets people\u2019s attention \u2014 people who may currently be on other teams. That can make a .500 team look better than a .500 team. That, you can sell. \u201cWe\u2019ve done kind of a good job keeping those (losing) thoughts at bay,\u201d Lopez said. \u201cWe realize the situation. But at the same time, we have a lot of young guys. We also have a lot of talented, and high BBIQ guys \u2014 very high basketball intelligence. But the East also has a couple of teams that are surpassing expectations. The Detroit Pistons (4-1), Indiana Pacers (3-2) and Orlando Magic (3-0) are a combined 10-3 against the West , and seven of those 10 wins have been against West teams that have winning records. Detroit, with a 4-2 record against all teams that are currently above .500, seems particularly legit. Andre Drummond\u2019s eye-opening improvement from the free throw line has been a part of the league\u2019s third biggest improvement in offensive efficiency, through Detroit has played more games against top-10 offenses (five) than against top-10 defenses (one) thus far. Things change quickly, but through the first eighth of the season, the East has been a little stronger and a more interesting than we expected. * * * Pace : Possessions per 48 minutes (League Rank) OffRtg : Points scored per 100 possessions (League Rank) DefRtg : Points allowed per 100 possessions (League Rank) NetRtg : Point differential per 100 possessions (League Rank) The league has averaged 101.1 possessions (per team) per 48 minutes and 104.0 points scored per 100 possessions this season. * * * NBA.com\u2019s Power Rankings, released every Monday during the season, are just one man\u2019s opinion. If you have an issue with the rankings, or have a question or comment for John Schuhmann, send him an e-mail or contact him via Twitter . * * *"},{"id":48584,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/morning-tip-waiting-game-continues-jahlil-okafor-philadelphia-76ers","date":"2017-11-06","title":"Waiting game continues for Jahlil Okafor, Philadelphia 76ers","content":" https:\/\/twitter.com\/Isaiah_Thomas\/status\/926073014952873984 * * * In our eternal, Twitter-driven search for villains accessible in 140 characters or less, there surely is someone to blame for Jahlil Okafor still being a Philadelphia 76er this morning. The third-year forward is clearly not a part of the Sixers\u2019 plans going forward. He\u2019s been in dry dock all season, having played in just one of Philly\u2019s first nine games . Sixers coach Brett Brown has made it clear that Okafor isn\u2019t going to be in the rotation \u2014 he\u2019s not only behind star center Joel Embiid on the depth chart, he also trails Richaun Holmes as well. And now that the Sixers have declined their fourth-year option on Okafor , making him an unrestricted free agent at season\u2019s end, the recriminations have begun in earnest. Yet a 30,000-foot view shows a 21-year-old whose career is still well in front of him, who\u2019ll get his chance soon enough to show for someone else the skills that made him a first-team all-America selection after his single college season at Duke, when he led the Blue Devils to the NCAA national championship. For now, though, an uncomfortable relationship with the team that took him third overall in the 2015 Draft remains. Okafor made it clear last week that he wants to be elsewhere \u2014 anywhere . But that won\u2019t be an easy lift. The Sixers are not going to let him go for nothing.  League sources indicate the Chicago Bulls and Atlanta Hawks are the most likely destinations for Okafor. But the Sixers are still holding out for at least a Draft pick, and could still opt to keep Okafor either as insurance against further injury to Embiid, or as a potential expiring contract to aggregate as the trade deadline nears. There\u2019s so much to unpack in the relationship between Okafor and the 76ers, who took him after Karl-Anthony Towns went to the Minnesota Timberwolves and the Los Angeles Lakers took D\u2019Angelo Russell second. You can start with that Draft night itself. The Sixers\u2019 instinct that night was not to go for Okafor, but to take a then-teenaged Latvian player who\u2019d played very well in the Spanish ACB League the previous two years. But the teenager, Kristaps Porzingis, refused to even meet with the Sixers , who were still in the throes of their rebuild (\u201cThe Process\u201d) and coming off of an 18-64 season. Porzingis\u2019 agent, Andy Miller, also had issues with the team and its then-GM Sam Hinkie. (The team\u2019s current GM, Bryan Colangelo, who\u2019s gotten a lot of the heat locally for how the 76ers have handled the Okafor situation of late, only said last week that the team would not fine Okafor for his comments about wanting out.) The 76ers could still have taken Porzingis. You don\u2019t have to have face-to-face meetings with a potential Draft pick to take someone. But teams are understandably reluctant to make a potential multi-million dollar investment into someone without having all available information in hand, from personal quirks and dislikes to up-to-date medical reports. So the Sixers passed on \u201cThe Unicorn\u201d and took Okafor (Porzingis went to New York with the next pick instead ). The problem for Philly was that it already had invested in its big man of the future, having taken Embiid third in the 2014 Draft . In addition, the Sixers\u2019 first rebuilding move was trading for the rights to center Nerlens Noel in 2013 from the New Orleans Pelicans . And they\u2019d also maneuvered to deal for the rights to power forward Dario Saric ( who was originally drafted by the Orlando Magic in 2014 ), who came over to the NBA last season. That gave Philly three young frontcourt players in which it had specific future plans on its roster before taking Okafor. There wasn\u2019t anywhere for him to play when he got to Philly. But Okafor has to own some of the dysfunction, too. He was not in shape his rookie season. In separate incidents his rookie season, he was involved in an assault outside a Boston nightclub , and was cited for speeding at 108 miles per hour across the Ben Franklin Bridge by local police. He did not exactly scream \u201cfundamental building block of the future\u201d with his off-court behavior. And yet, with Embiid still rehabbing from foot surgeries and out for the season, Okafor still averaged 17.5 points and 7 rebounds as a rookie , showing he was worthy offensively of a steady diet of post-ups. Defense was another matter entirely , but let\u2019s get real: individual defense, or the lack thereof, is no longer much of a consideration in today\u2019s NBA. Okafor may be bad defensively, but \u2026 compared to whom? The league has made it clear what it values with its all-offense all the time rules changes of the last generation. Golden State is a terrific defensive team, to be sure. But the Warriors became the Warriors because of, first, the \u201cSplash Brothers\u2019\u201d incredible shooting prowess. That tilted the board completely. Draymond Green is a great two-way player and Andre Iguodala made selflessness a hallmark in the Bay. But it all started with Stephen Curry and KlayThompson making shots at an historic rate . Add to that Kevin Durant in his mold-busting prime, and you have an unstoppable offensive force. Teams aren\u2019t trying to emulate the Warriors\u2019 defensive principles \u2014 they\u2019re trying to match their firepower. Anyway, back to Okafor. His days in Philly were numbered when Embiid finally got on the court last season. Any four who plays alongside \u201cThe Process\u201d best have some inside-outside to his game, and Okafor has shot exactly six 3-pointers in his first two-plus NBA seasons \u2014 and none since that rookie season. Because of that, understandably, Brown gave Saric a ton of minutes toward the end of last season, when Saric make a strong run at Kia Rookie of the Year. Okafor, on the other hand, didn\u2019t play in the Sixers\u2019 last 11 games of 2016-17 . The Sixers were close to a deal last February that would have sent Okafor to Portland . But sources indicated, then and now, that the Blazers changed their plans and went in instead on a deal with Denver that brought them Jusuf Nurkic in exchange for Mason Plumlee. Deals fall through all the time, but this looked especially bad because the 76ers told Okafor to stay home and not go on a road trip with them since they believed a deal was imminent. This year, the idea was to showcase Okafor during the preseason , and Brown did give him some burn off the bench \u2014 but not a ton. So, where can Philly send him? The Sixers are reluctant to just cut Okafor loose, knowing it will take Celtics boss Danny Ainge about 30 seconds to scarf him up and put him into the injured player exception Boston has for Gordon Hayward. (The two teams haven\u2019t been able to come together on a trade.) Okafor\u2019s knee is sound and he\u2019s in the best shape of his young career. Some have trotted out the usual suspects: Phoenix and New York and other rebuilding teams. But those teams have their own problems and their own young frontcourt players (Marquese Chriss and Dragan Bender for the Suns; Porzingis and Enes Kanter with the Knicks) who\u2019ll need all the minutes they can get to further develop. That is also, it says here, selling Okafor short \u2014 that all he can be is a stats hunter on a bad team. But the Sixers also don\u2019t want to add any salary to get Okafor off the books. They have every intention of extending forward Robert Covington as soon as they are able \u2014 Nov. 15 \u2014 and aren\u2019t going past that in new expenditures this season. But teams are asking Philly to take back more salary in exchange for Okafor\u2019s now expiring $4.9 million contract. And, if it doesn\u2019t work with Chicago or Atlanta, there aren\u2019t a lot of obvious other places the Sixers could send him. A lot of solid and\/or promising teams like Charlotte, New Orleans (which had interest in the past in Okafor) and Detroit are over the cap and perilously close to the tax threshold, and no one is going to go over it to take a chance that Okafor might be better than he showed in Philly. And good teams already paying the tax this season are obviously not in the mix. Jahlil Okafor will get a shot, somewhere, to play again. But he may have to wait, yet again. * * * MORE MORNING TIP:  Young Lakers see bright future | DA\u2019s Top 15 Rankings | Your questions on Detroit\u2019s start, Cavs\u2019 woes | Q&A: C.J.
