( And, hi, Olivia! Hi Kevin! ) \u201cWe\u2019re gonna try to squeeze it in there sometime soon,\u201d Kent Bazemore said Saturday. The Hawks\u2019 forward could go viral in the good old days \u2014 just two or three years ago \u2014 when Atlanta was a contender in the Eastern Conference, a feel-good collection of selfless players, coached to get better by Mike Budenholzer and his teaching-first staff. The ball moved and the 3-pointers were copious and the Hawks won 60 games in 2014-15, sending four of their five starters \u2014 Al Horford, Paul Millsap, Jeff Teague and Kyle Korver \u2014 to that year\u2019s All-Star Game. That was then. Now, the Hawks push cricket tacos.  The protein-rich delicacy is just one food offering this year\u2019s team is selling in Philips Arena, to try and keep fans happy while they watch a team that no longer has any of those All-Stars, restructured its front office last summer and has embraced a full rebuild under first-year General Manager Travis Schlenk \u2014 Schlenk taking over Budenholzer\u2019s duties at the request of Hawks\u2019 ownership. That new group, which bought the team at the height of its best play in \u201915 , watched the team\u2019s win total drop from 60 to 48 to 43 last season, which concluded with a first-round loss to the Washington Wizards . Barring an unexpected resurgence this season, Atlanta will be hard-pressed to get to 43 this season. Millsap is now with the Denver Nuggets. Horford is on the Boston Celtics. Teague, traded to Indiana in 2016, is now with the Minnesota Timberwolves and Korver is with the Cleveland Cavaliers. That leaves a handful of vets like Bazemore and point guard Dennis Schroeder, who were there for the good old days, and a bunch of kids learning on the job. Not too many Gazes are in the offing in the near future. \u201cFor me, I\u2019m a super fiery player,\u201d Bazemore said. \u201cI\u2019ve had to work on controlling my emotions. There\u2019s so many people watching, and thinking less of yourself in certain situations. Things are looking up. In every game we\u2019ve played this year in every form or fashion we\u2019ve given ourselves a chance. Beat Dallas, went down to Miami and had a chance to win there, Brooklyn the same, being up 18 on Charlotte on their opening night. \u201cWe\u2019ve shown glimpses of being a good team; it\u2019s not like we\u2019re going into these arenas and getting blown out by 50 every night.\u201d But, honestly, the losses are part of the plan this year. The worst thing you can be in the NBA is mediocre, and that\u2019s where the Hawks were. Majority owner Tony Ressler had to be convinced to let Millsap go, but he signed off on not re-signing Millsap, and then went all-in on Process South, replacing former GM Wes Wilcox in May \u2014 who remains with the franchise as a consultant \u2014 with Schlenk, who was the assistant GM with the Warriors the last five years. \u201cWell, we had two choices, the way I saw it,\u201d Ressler said Friday, in the new owners\u2019\/VIP digs, which are hard off the new Hawks Bar that is directly behind the baseline , steps off the floor \u2014 one of the many parts of the Philips renovation, which is scheduled to conclude next year.  \u201cWe never had the choice of being a contender. We weren\u2019t,\u201d Ressler said. \u201cI saw the team go from 60 wins to 48 to 43. And we didn\u2019t make many changes going from 60 to 48 to 43. We thought we made additions. Let\u2019s just say I concluded, with Travis\u2019 help, with Bud\u2019s help, I concluded that we were not going in the right direction. \u201cTruly, there are three options in the NBA, I would argue: being a contender, being a competitive team, and being young and fun. At least that would be my opinion. And we didn\u2019t have the option of being a contender. So we could be competitive, or more competitive, and maybe, shall we say, with a whole bunch of higher-priced vets that made us older and made our payroll less flexible, and made our future more cloudy.\u201d During an explosive summer of free agency and trades leaguewide, Schlenk worked along the margins, getting involved in deals that sent Dwight Howard to Charlotte for Miles Plumlee and Marco Belinelli ; working into the Danilo Gallinari trade with the Clippers and Nuggets by taking on Jamal Crawford from L.A. (the Hawks waived him shortly thereafter and he signed with the Wolves). But Schlenk also got a 2018 first-round pick from the Clippers in the deal, giving him three total in next year\u2019s Draft \u2014 Atlanta already has a Lottery-protected 2018 first-round pick from Minnesota \u2014 to add to the two 2019 first-rounders the Hawks have in hand. The Hawks gave former Spurs center Dewayne Dedmon a short deal (two years, $12 million, second year team option), but other than that, they\u2019re committed to building around their young guys: Schroeder, second-year wings Taurean Prince and DeAndre Bembry, and rookie big man John Collins. \u201cFor me, at least, I can\u2019t speak for other guys, but losing games, I just try to think we\u2019re playing with the best of the world every night,\u201d Collins said after the Hawks lost their sixth game in their first seven Sunday. \u201cIt\u2019s not going to be easy. Nobody\u2019s going to give you anything.\u201d Collins carries the poker chips around for the team flights, and gets the Snickers on the late-night snack calls and tries to repeat the pattern of sudden improvement he showed from his freshman to his sophomore season at Wake Forest . Schlenk was, as he puts it, \u201cin NBA La-La Land\u201d at Golden State. Now, he can\u2019t just get lost going to games and getting ready for Drafts; he must sell the rebuilding vision in a city that was slow to warm to the Hawks, but embraced the \u201cTrue to Atlanta\u201d motto during the team\u2019s run to the Eastern Conference finals . \u201cThat\u2019s the hard part, with the fans,\u201d Schlenk said. \u201cI would say that 90 percent of the people I see in Atlanta, meet in Atlanta, say \u2018hey, love what you\u2019re doing, needs to be done.\u2019 There\u2019s another 10 percent of \u2018what are you doing?\u2019 But I think just as far as with Bud and the ownership group, it\u2019s just constantly reminding them, listen, it\u2019s painful right now. But there\u2019s light at the end of the tunnel. We have five Draft picks the next two years, first-round picks. It\u2019s my job to, hopefully, get four of those right.\u201d Budenholzer came to Atlanta from San Antonio in 2013 under former general manager Danny Ferry. After Ferry lost his job over racially insensitive remarks he made in a pre-Draft meeting in 2014 \u2014 with people subsequently taking sides all over the organization during what became an internal power struggle involving the team\u2019s previous majority owners \u2014 the power vacuum created led to Budenholzer gaining control over all the franchise\u2019s basketball decisions. But the devolving record and the new ownership group led by Ressler didn\u2019t give Budenholzer much chance to retain both jobs. \u201cI think Mike felt he was a great head coach,\u201d Ressler said. \u201cI tried to convince him and I think he realized fully that being the GM is a full-time job. So why does anyone on earth think they can do two extraordinarily difficult jobs? And I believe Bud saw that very clearly. And to this minute, I think what Bud wanted above everything else was a great GM who knew more about player personnel than he could or did. It\u2019s not a part-time job. And anyone who thinks it is, I think makes a big mistake. \u201cAnd being a great head coach that is extraordinary in player development, and where players literally \u2014 which is not that common \u2014 there are not that many ways to distinguish yourselves, to differentiate yourselves as a head coach in this league. But making players think they can come here to get better, I absolutely believe is one of those. But that\u2019s not a part-time (bleeping) job. That\u2019s a tough job. I think Bud, and I certainly had a strong view, as you might imagine, I said we need a great GM and we need a great head coach. I thought we had a great head coach. And I thought we had a GM that was not great, that was not experienced, who was not top dog. It\u2019s just two jobs.\u201d Budenholzer acknowledges it was \u201cnot easy\u201d to give up the VP job and its decision-making authority. But this is how the Hawks are organized now, and he\u2019s made his peace with it. \u201cIt\u2019s a change,\u201d he said. \u201cAnd I think that can be a positive, where either I have to think through things even more deeply and be more convicted or more capable of articulating why it is something is important to me and have everybody understand it. And there\u2019s going to be people who say \u2018I completely, totally disagree, and we\u2019re not going to do that.\u2019 And I\u2019ll grow from it, and hopefully the organization grows from it. But when you\u2019ve kind of been in that position and you do have passion and you do have vision, hopefully all for good, it\u2019s certainly going to be different. But it\u2019s a good different. It\u2019s a good change.\u201d Schlenk tread lightly the first few weeks after taking the GM job. He couldn\u2019t go my way or the highway. This was a proud group of guys who\u2019d done great work in making the Hawks a legit exciting team to watch for the first time in a long time. \u201cWe sat down, probably the first day I got the job here, we went to dinner \u2014 (Chief Executive Officer Steve) Koonin, (Chief Operating Officer) Thad Sheely and Bud and I all went to dinner,\u201d Schlenk said. \u201cAnd then the next day Bud and I sat down for three or four hours and just talked about different things. And really, I kind of knew in my mind what I wanted to do with this. \u201cAny time you come in, you kind of want to put your stamp on it. But he had been here and it was his stamp and he had emotional connections to all of these guys that I didn\u2019t have. So it took, I got hired first of June, end of May, But I would say it took two or three weeks of, I wasn\u2019t assertive at all. I would just sit back and have conversations. But we kind of channeled the conversations in the direction I wanted to. And he knew.\u201d A week before the Draft, Budenholzer went to Schlenk\u2019s office and told him he was all in. But, because coaches are still judged on their won-loss record, it was no shock that Budenholzer still argued for keeping Millsap, the Hawks\u2019 remaining All-Star and his best all-around player last season. \u201cAnd Tony (also) wants to win,\u201d Schlenk said. \u201cHe doesn\u2019t want to go through this. But I would just constantly say, \u2018listen. You guys won (43) games. You want to win (43) games again?\u2019 I get this will be painful. Believe me, the first four games, I\u2019m sitting up there miserable.\u201d It leaves Budenholzer to focus on what has been the team\u2019s strength since he got there \u2014 a strength that gave former Hawks\u2019 assistant coach Kenny Atkinson a shot at the top job in Brooklyn \u2014 player development. It is a mantra of the coaches in Atlanta that everyone, no matter how long they\u2019ve been in the league, can get better. The proof, ironically, is in the deals that many former Hawks have gotten from other teams, from Millsap\u2019s big contract with Denver to Tim Hardaway, Jr.\u2019s $72 million deal with the New York Knicks. \u201cOrganizationally, this is the way we\u2019re organized now, and this gives us the best chance going forward to have a chance in Atlanta to have success,\u201d Budenholzer said. \u201cI\u2019m passionate about coaching. I love coaching. But I\u2019m passionate about everything. And I think, I believe in our ownership, I believe in all the changes we\u2019ve made and what we\u2019re doing going forward.\u201d The Hawks opened their new practice facility, the Emory Sports Medicine Complex , last week. The $50 million complex, about 15 minutes northeast of downtown, will house the front offices and medical staff, with space for a P3 facility in the building . Several players trained at the original P3 in California over the past few offseasons. The team is also building an arena in nearby College Park that will open in 2019-20 for its new G League team . For now, that team \u2013 the Erie Bayhawks \u2013 is playing in Pennsylvania this season and next.  Meanwhile, the $192.5 million renovation of Philips Arena will continue through the season. The lower concourse is being broken up, with the single wall of suites on one side of the building now being broken up. The 15 \u201cbunker suites\u201d and other seating that were state of the art when the building opened in 1999 have fallen victim to the times and the current state of the team. The Hawks plan to create \u201cfuture seating\u201d in their building \u2014 theatre seats, loge seats \u2014 they went to Las Vegas and found that pool events at casino hotels are now driving up to 20 percent of revenues there. There won\u2019t be pools at Philips. It\u2019s the thinking outside of the traditional game-presentation box that the Hawks hope will make games more than just about winning and losing. \u201cThis is entertainment,\u201d Koonin said. \u201cThe line between entertainment and sports is more blurred than it\u2019s ever been before. So we\u2019ve got Run the Jewels playing at halftime . We\u2019ve got every minute programmed, no different than HBO or TNT \u2026 and we\u2019re young. People understand. This is a town that understands, and craves a championship, and that there\u2019s a price to winning a championship. And sometimes you have to take a step back. We\u2019ve been in the playoffs for 10 years. We\u2019ve had a lot of success. We have not gotten our goal yet.\u201d A renovated Philips will be part of a renovated complex \u2014 \u201cit\u2019s not often that you have a 35-acre hole in the ground in downtown Atlanta,\u201d Ressler said that includes Philips Arena and the Falcons\u2019 new stadium, Mercedes-Benz Stadium \u2014 and will, everyone in the city seems to hope, sometime soon include \u201cThe Gulch,\u201d an undeveloped parcel of land that is chopped up by railroad tracks and looks as bad as the name sounds. But renovations, to be done well, must be done right the first time \u2014 measure twice, cut once, and all that. Ressler \u2014 in Riyadh and Abu Dhabi Thursday, Atlanta on Friday \u2014 has learned he must slow his own roll and accept the down year or two that awaits. \u201cWinning a championship, winning 60 games, would be great \u2014 and, actually, preferable,\u201d Ressler said. \u201cBut, to us, it\u2019s a package. The idea of building a practice facility and refurbishing the arena and sending a message to your fan base that you\u2019re trying to go in the right directions, I personally believe all are required. It\u2019s not one of the three. Frankly, what we\u2019ve learned is, if you just try to show people oh, we\u2019re redoing the arena and we\u2019re building the practice facility, and we\u2019re bringing the G League team in, but we\u2019re not focusing on both our payroll and the team on the court, you lose. \u201cSo, to me, you\u2019ve got to send a clear message: we\u2019re all of the above. And, we are \u2026 my wife (actress Jami Gertz) likes to say \u2018don\u2019t be so competitive.\u2019 Everything\u2019s competitive \u2026 but our view is, you\u2019ve got to send a message that the franchise is going in the right direction.\u201d * * * MORE MORNING TIP: Harrington finds new career in medical marijuana | DA\u2019s Top 15 rankings | Morning Tip mailbag: How far can Pelicans go?  * * * Longtime NBA reporter, columnist and Naismith Memorial Basketball Hall of Famer David Aldridge is an analyst for TNT. Just ask mid-90s Magic fans, turn-of-the-century Kings faithful, or witnesses of Seven Seconds or Less in Phoenix. You can lump Grizzlies fans of the 2010s into that group, because it\u2019s hard to find a stronger local connection than the one that exists between Memphis and its NBA franchise of recent years. The team and its city take pride in \u201cGrit and Grind,\u201d a brand of basketball that wasn\u2019t always pretty, but effective enough to earn seven straight postseason trips and a trio of 50-win seasons. They rallied behind an underrated cast headlined by a non-All-Star point guard ( Mike Conley ), castoff forward (Zach Randolph) and late-blooming center ( Marc Gasol ). That era appeared to be in danger after the 2017 offseason , when the Grizzlies bid farewell to Randolph. It was hard to imagine \u201cGrit and Grind\u201d without the fan favorite forward, who bulldozed his way to 16.8 points and 1.0 2 rebounds per game in his eight seasons with Memphis. Ditto for the loss of Tony Allen, a limited-but-beloved guard who made life miserable for elite scorers. Fast forward to Day 12 of the 2017-18 regular season, and the Grizzlies are sitting pretty at 5-1. It\u2019s their best start to a season since 2014-15 \u2014 the same year Memphis advanced all the way to the Western Conference finals. The faces have changed. The identity has not. Memphis\u2019s stubborn refusal to fade was on full display against Houston on Saturday night. Facing the ultimate example of run-and-gun basketball, the Grizzlies doubled down on their own style and showed why they still have a place at the Western Conference table. They limited the Rockets to 89 points on 37.7-percent shooting, well below their early-season marks of 106.3 points per game at a 45.1-percent clip. After their 103-98 victory , the supposedly endangered Grizzlies now sport the best record (5-1) in the league. The cast of characters is different, but the formula remains the same. Entering Saturday night\u2019s game, Memphis ranked eighth in defensive rating at 98.3 points allowed per 100 possessions, which would be their best mark since 2012-13. They have compensated for Randolph\u2019s absence partly through Gasol (25.0 ppg, 10.8 rpg) and partly through a committee of energetic role players. Tyreke Evans will never fulfill the promise he showed in his Kia Rookie of the Year campaign, but he gives the Grizzlies an extra playmaker who rebounds extremely well for a perimeter player. James Ennis III and Jarell Martin provide energy and more rebounding at the forward spots. Mario Chalmers adds a much-needed dash of passing and shooting. They might be even better if Chandler Parsons can build on his long awaited coming-out party on Saturday. The seventh-year forward, who played just 34 games last season, poured in 24 points on 9-of-11 shooting in 19 minutes. Without that, the Grizzlies likely don\u2019t survive a rare off-night from both Gasol and Conley (14 points, 5-of-18 FG combined). When healthy, Parsons gives Memphis the third scorer it needs to complement the Gasol-Conley duo. Without him, Gasol\u2019s admirably crafted 3-point stroke (43.5 percent) is the lone outside threat opponents consistently respect. Even so, the Grizzlies aren\u2019t fretting about offensive flaws when its strengths \u2014 defense and execution \u2014 can carry the day if everyone buys in. So far, they are. Memphis is yielding the fewest points off turnovers per game (12.6) and the second-fewest points in the paint (37.6). Again, it\u2019s still ridiculously early \u2014 just two weeks into the season, at a point in the calendar when the NBA is typically just starting. They\u2019ve been particularly impressive on the offensive end, ranking among the league leaders in an array of categories entering Friday\u2019s game including points per 100 possessions ( second ), 3-point shooting ( first ), assist ratio ( second ) and pace ( fourth ).  \u201cWe\u2019re starting to play offensively consistently the right way in terms of not settling and understanding that we want to attack early and the ball is really hopping,\u201d Orlando coach Frank Vogel told Magic.com last week. \u201cWe\u2019re scoring the ball well and shooting the ball well as a result of the ball movement and the quality of our shots.\u201d If those words sounds strange coming from a coach who emphasized defense and physicality in his previous stint with the Pacers, they shouldn\u2019t. Vogel expressed a \u201cgreat desire\u201d to play up-tempo basketball on his first day on the job in 2016. It took them a season to get there, but the Magic are making up for lost time. They shredded the Spurs\u2019 fourth-ranked defense on Friday, shooting 57.1 percent with 11 3s. The key players in their early season success \u2014 Evan Fournier, Aaron Gordon and Nikola Vucevic \u2014 combined for 56 points on 23-for-32 shooting, and Jonathon Simmons scored 17 in 23 minutes off the bench against his old team. All told, it was the kind of clinic the Spurs have been conducting for years.  \u201cIt\u2019s too early to make any big judgments,\u201d Vogel said after the Magic\u2019s third game, and it still applies following their fifth. \u201cBut it\u2019s an early positive sign for us. Everybody is playing basketball the right way, thinking extra pass and playing for each other. That\u2019s how chemistry is established.\u201d And perhaps, a few months down the road, an end to Orlando\u2019s lengthy postseason drought. The Russian billionaire has been an infrequent spectator in recent years as the Nets tumbled from playoff team to worst record in the league, and he has for a while been open to selling a minority share. Instead, he will eventually become the minority owner, retaining 20 percent of the franchise after Tsai takes control in 2021. The deal is for the franchise only and not Barclays Center, the $1 billion arena that opened in 2012. There\u2019s the macro purpose of winning games, entertaining fans and making the playoffs. Then there\u2019s the micro purpose that actually might wind up being more instrumental to the Bucks\u2019 long-term fortunes and ambitions. That is, the ongoing development of Giannis Antetokounmpo as Milwaukee\u2019s cornerstone player and the NBA\u2019s Unicorn Flavor of the Month. Antetokounmpo is the real deal and has been for a while. When the franchise\u2019s sparkling new facility opens next fall \u2014 two blocks and a world away from the old Milwaukee Arena they dusted off for their throwback Thursday game against the Celtics \u2014 it rightly will begin its useful life as the House That Giannis Built. Antetokounmpo\u2019s remarkable start to the 2017-18 schedule has people chronicling his achievements and taking his pulse after every game. Yes, he leads the Bucks in minutes, points, rebounds, assists, steals, player efficiency rating (an astounding 37.3) and usage rate (34.8 percent). And yes, no Milwaukee player ever has scored more through the first five games of a season; Antetokounmpo\u2019s 175 points moved him past Kareem Abdul-Jabbar, who opened 1970-71 with 171 through five performances (before adding 81 more in the next two games). It\u2019s a tough way to go through a season, though, with folks monitoring his every move and running the math every time Antetokounmpo posts his crooked numbers. At some point he will fall off his record-setting pace for this, that or the other thing. The Bucks will have doubled or tripled the sample size \u2014 five games represents a mere 6.1 percent of their schedule \u2014 and everyone can get busy with the short check list that really will define his and his team\u2019s success. 1. Did Milwaukee win? 2. Did Antetokounmpo finish the game healthy? 3. How did this opponent defend against and\/or attack him? Antetokounmpo knows that his status as an All-Star, Kia MVP candidate or future Mt. Rushmore figure depends first and foremost on No. 1. He\u2019ll only max out his individual potential if he can make sure the Bucks max out theirs. No. 2 is essential, too, particularly for a team that has dealt with multiple injuries in recent seasons, most notably Khris Middleton\u2019s torn hamstring a year ago and Jabari Parker\u2019s serial ACL blowouts . Hardly anyone gets out of The Association unscathed, but let\u2019s hope for our own curious and selfish sake that the \u201cGreek Freak\u201d stays closer to LeBron James-and Kevin Garnett-healthy for most of his career.As for No. 3, that\u2019s straight basketball business and it was on display against Boston Thursday . The Celtics already had suffered at Antetokounmpo\u2019s hand in their home opener last week when he notched 37 points and 13 rebounds in Milwaukee\u2019s 108-100 victory . But then, that was the tail end of a back-to-back after they started in Cleveland 24 hours earlier \u2014 and Boston still was rattled from the sudden loss of free agent All-Star Gordon Hayward\u2019s services for the season. This time, the Celtics had time and focus to prep, and coach Brad Stevens changed up one specific matchup: Instead of having forward Jaylen Brown guard Antetokounmpo, he gave that chore to big man Al Horford. With the 6-foot-10, 240-pound Horford crowding Antetokounmpo and with various Boston helpers bumping or running at him, the Bucks\u2019 young star had a far more disjointed experience on his way to 28 points, 10 rebounds and seven assists. Horford met Antetokounmpo on the stats sheet, too, with 27 points, nine boards and four assists \u2014 and stayed close while teammates filled the lane to take away Antetokounmpo\u2019s space. \u201cTeams know he wants to get to the paint, teams know that\u2019s where he\u2019s most effective,\u201d Milwaukee point guard Malcolm Brogdon said. \u201cWhether it\u2019s finishing or finding guys, he touches the paint first. So they\u2019re bringing five guys in and forcing him to pass it or forcing him to take contested shots.\u201d Compared to the Bucks\u2019 first game against Boston, when they got to the foul line 30 times, they earned only 14 this time. As specific to Thursday\u2019s game as this might seem a day later, it really serves as an example of what Antetokounmpo and his guys will face over the next 77 games. In this era of three (or more) All-Star caliber teammates on the top contenders, the \u201cGreek Freak\u201d is the proverbial head-of-the-snake type for Milwaukee. He has had only limited help through the season\u2019s first two weeks. Middleton, the Bucks\u2019 best shooter and second-most talented player, is an inexplicable 3-for-19 on 3-pointers. Besides him (15.2 ppg), Brogdon (15.8) and Tony Snell (11.0), no one else is averaging more than 6.8 points, five rebounds or 3.2 field goal attempts. \u201cYou could tell night to night the other defenders pay more attention to me,\u201d Antetokoumpo said. \u201cYou can see from the start that everybody loads and they close gaps so I don\u2019t have a lot of room to go. I know moving forward that\u2019s going to happen. I just got to stay disciplined and trust our offense, try to move the ball and I know the ball is going to find me back.\u201d Antetokounmpo and Brogdon agreed that the other Bucks can help him most by hitting shots when the point forward\u2019s passes find them. There\u2019s no better way to drag defenders off him. The other imperative for Milwaukee is to lighten Antetokounmpo\u2019s load overall. It\u2019s not just his overall court time \u2014 a league high 39.2 minutes nightly \u2014 but the grind in each of those minutes. Gutting out five games is one thing; pushing through the next 77 or so at his current level is asking for burnout. \u201cWe have to make sure he doesn\u2019t have to work that hard to get his shots,\u201d Brogdon said Thursday night. \u201cHe doesn\u2019t need to drive inside every time. We need to drive inside for him sometimes to get him easy shots. \u201cHe\u2019s worked hard. That\u2019s sort of his style of play. But as the season goes on, there are going to be games where he\u2019s a little bit tired. Those are the games where we\u2019ll need to work hard to get him the easy shots.\u201d No one has seen Antetokounmpo tucker out yet. Before exiting the cramped, home-locker-room-for-a-night at the MECCA, he chugged some sort of healthy energy drink, wrinkled up his face at the taste, then looked fresh heading into the Milwaukee chill. Then again, there\u2019s only one Energizer bunny in the NBA and he still plays in Oklahoma City. \u201cI think Giannis is next in line in terms of guys who have that type of motor,\u201d Brogdon said, \u201cbut it\u2019s tough to play that way every night.\u201d Steve Aschburner has written about the NBA since 1980. Then we give it an overall grade on a scale of 1-5 Robert Horrys, named for the patron saint of last-second answered prayers. * * * There are two undefeated teams remaining 10 days into the regular season. One is the Kawhi Leonard-less San Antonio Spurs. The other is the remodeled LA Clippers, thanks to Blake Griffin\u2019s buzzer-beating heroics on Thursday night. The eighth-year forward sank a 3-pointer from the left side as time expired to bump the Clippers to 4-0 to start 2017-18 . The dramatic victory came at the expense of the Portland Trail Blazers, who were 3-1 entering last night\u2019s game. C.J. McCollum appeared to have given his team the final edge with a go-ahead jumper and a free throw in the final minute, but Griffin trumped that with the 3-pointer that proved to be the difference. DIFFICULTY: Griffin said the final play was designed for him to attack the basket, but that Portland\u2019s defense negated that option. Instead, he was forced to navigate all the way around teammate Patrick Beverley, using him as a casual screen to create space for the sliver of time he needed. Even then, Griffin felt compelled to give a pump fake, but Al-Farouq Aminu still contested the shot well from Griffin\u2019s right side. Shooting from distance after a momentum-killing pump fake is not easy, but Griffin\u2019s shot was pure proof of how much work the former Slam Dunk Contest champion has put into his outside shot. GAME SITUATION: The Clippers faced quite the letdown after leading by as many as 10 points in the second half. Griffin was the reason Los Angeles survived Portland\u2019s comeback attempt, as he scored 16 of his game-high 25 points in the fourth quarter . Still, McCollum\u2019s final three points had the Blazers poised for a two-point victory, which would have been especially frustrating after how hotly contested the final few possessions were. Clippers guard Austin Rivers dislocated his finger on the previous possession and earned an offensive foul in the process, forcing Los Angeles to foul McCollum. Luckily for the Clippers, the 92-percent free throw shooter missed one of his two free throws, leaving Griffin the chance to put the game away in regulation. CELEBRATION: Griffin defiantly ran the opposite direction and into his jubilant teammates, who mock-restrained him as he marched about in the now-silenced Moda Center. If there was ever a scene that depicted Griffin\u2019s place as the undisputed star of the LA Clippers, this was it. GRADE: Every win is big in the Western Conference, where good teams run the risk of not being good enough. Thanks to Griffin, the Clippers have an early lead in that race. Many wondered how Los Angeles would perform after trading Chris Paul to Houston. Griffin\u2019s emphatic answer on Thursday night: pretty darn good. Three-and-a-half Horrys. Warriors spokesman Raymond Ridder said Thursday that the beloved Attles, who turns 81 on Nov. 7, is doing fine and will return to Oracle Arena as soon as he can in the near future. Details of his condition were not disclosed, the team said. The Warriors will continue with their plans to honor him during Friday\u2019s home game against the Washington Wizards. Attles bobblehead dolls will be a giveaway and players will wear shooting shirts featuring his likeness. He is a longtime staple at games with a regular seat on press row high above the court in Oracle Arena, though Attles missed a stretch of time last season when he was not well. He returned to see Golden State win the franchise\u2019s second championship in three years against Cleveland. Attles is in his 58th year with the Warriors, having played in Wilt Chamberlain\u2019s 100-point game on March 2, 1962 . He coached the Warriors to the 1975 title, then watched as Stephen Curry and Co. won 40 years later in 2015. Attles scored 17 points on 8-for-8 shooting for the Philadelphia Warriors during Chamberlain\u2019s 100-point performance. Attles coached Rick Barry the day he scored 64 against Portland on March 26, 1974. He then loved witnessing Klay Thompson score a career-best 60 points in three quarters in a 142-106 victory over Indiana last December \u2013 the highest Warriors scoring performance since Barry\u2019s. A fifth-round draft pick by the Warriors in 1960, Attles was honored during the postseason in June along with Hubie Brown as co-recipients of the 2017 Chuck Daly Lifetime Achievement Award from the National Basketball Coaches Association."},{"id":48694,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/hang-time-podcast-washington-wizards-john-wall-lonzo-ball","date":"2017-10-26","title":"Hang Time Podcast: Wizards' West Coast trip with Candace Buckner","content":"Candace Buckner of The Washington Post joins us to talk about the Washington Wizards\u2019 loss in L.A., their upcoming matchup with Golden State on Friday , and much more. Then John Schuhmann joins to take a look at how Oklahoma City is distributing shots early in the season. * * * Be sure to subscribe to the Hang Time Podcast on Apple Podcasts or iHeart Radio for new episodes every Thursday this season!"},{"id":43516,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/milwaukee-bucks-return-mecca-face-boston-celtics","date":"2017-10-26","title":"MECCA forever holds special memories, time in Milwaukee Bucks' lore","content":"MILWAUKEE \u2013 Think of this as an old timer\u2019s game. Except in place of the aging basketball stars of yesteryear, this one will feature the chilly drafts, creaking hinges and narrow concourses of a long-retired NBA arena spiffed up for one last game. And one lasting stroll down memory lane. When the Milwaukee Bucks play host to the Boston Celtics on Thursday, they\u2019ll take #TBT to a whole new level. Rather than staging the game at their usual venue, the BMO Harris Bradley Center, the Bucks will clash with their fellow Eastern Conference wannabes at the old Milwaukee Arena, which later became known nationally (for a colorful reason to be explored below) as \u201cthe MECCA.\u201d The Bucks played in that building for 20 years, from their inception in 1968-69 through the 1987-88 season. A $10 million, barrel-roofed state-of-the-art facility when it opened in 1950, where the Milwaukee Hawks (before moving to St. Louis and eventually Atlanta) were the first NBA tenants for four seasons through 1954-55, the Arena over the past three decades became the home of the University of Wisconsin-Milwaukee Panthers and the Milwaukee Admirals of the American Hockey League . But because Milwaukee seems to only add downtown sports facilities without subtracting any \u2013 the Arena sits immediately to the south of the Bradley Center , which sits immediately to the south of the new, $524 million facility set to open for the Bucks\u2019 2018-19 season \u2013 this one was available when ideas got tossed around for commemorating the current franchise\u2019s 50th season. \u201cWe started talking about the possibility of doing a game there probably three or four years ago,\u201d said Dustin Godsey, the Bucks\u2019 chief marketing officer. \u201cWe\u2019d heard repeatedly as we started looking at a new building so much from fans about what it was like to see a game there. \u201cWe were digging into opportunities to celebrate and this became kind of a no-brainer to us to see if it was possible.\u201d The NBA had to sign off on the idea, of course, because this isn\u2019t 1968 or even \u201888. The Celtics hardly are a mundane opponent, but the Bucks\u2019 season-ticket base of approximately 7,500 meant that the team\u2019s most valued customers could be accommodated in the old arena. It boasts a capacity now of 12,700 compared to the familiar 10,938 figure that meant \u201csellout\u201d when the Bucks and the Marquette University Golden Eagles (then known as the Warriors) called MECCA it home. * Photo gallery:  Iconic MECCA court returns to Milwaukee Arena But there\u2019s still no upper bowl of seating. Locker rooms and concession stands have been updated since the \u201880s, yet it undeniably is an old arena, with all the expected limitations and charm. \u201cIt\u2019s fun for me \u2014 I\u2019m not originally from Milwaukee \u2014 just to see thee fans get excited and relive those great teams and memories,\u201d Godsey said. \u201cThere are so many people who heard from their parents about going to games at MECCA or were kids 30 years ago. For them now to be able to say, \u2018My dad took me and these were the seats we sat in,\u2019 and to be able to take their kids, that\u2019s going to be really special.\u201d Bob Pettit, the Hall of Fame power forward , played his Rookie of the Year season at the Milwaukee Arena in 1954-55 before moving with the Hawks to St. Louis and winning MVPs in \u201856 and \u201859. From 1955-68, the building\u2019s chief basketball tenant was Marquette. Al McGuire colorfully coached future NBA players such as George Thompson, Dean Meminger, Jim Chones, Larry McNeil, Maurice Lucas, Earl Tatum and Lloyd Walton, and led the school to two Finals Fours and the NCAA title in 1977. Despite the 13-year gap between NBA teams, though, the pro game\u2019s most illustrious names passed through the Arena\u2019s doors. Tom Enlund, longtime Bucks beat writer for the Milwaukee Journal Sentinel , did the research and found that 48 of the league\u2019s 50 Greatest Players had played there. The two exceptions: David Robinson and Shaquille O\u2019Neal, who got to the NBA in 1989 and 1992 respectively, after the Bucks had moved into Bradley Center. Guess who else played there: Elvis Presley, The Beatles, The Rolling Stones, The Doors, The Who, Led Zeppelin, Jethro Tull and Jimi Hendrix. As well as Frank Sinatra, Ray Charles, Neil Diamond and Luciano Pavarotti. In addition to Stevie Ray Vaughn, George Thorogood, Frank Zappa, Green Day, Stone Temple Pilots, Matchbox Twenty, Maroon 5 and Lil\u2019 Wayne. Every President from Truman through Obama has appeared there, as did former Minnesota governor Jesse (The Body) Ventura in his pro wrestling days, along with untold circus performers and roller-derby queens. So, for that matter, did Wayne Embry. \u201cWhere are they playing?\u201d Embry said by phone this week. \u201cOh my goodness. I\u2019ll be damned.\u201d Embry, most famous as the first black general manager of a major U.S. professional sports team when he was promoted to that post by the Bucks in 1972, got his first glimpse of the Arena while in college. His school, Miami of Ohio, had faced Marquette there. He returned in his 11th and final NBA season after being picked from Boston in the 1968 expansion draft. On Oct. 16 of that year, Embry scored 15 points in the Bucks\u2019 debut game , a loss to the Chicago Bulls in front of 8,467 fans at the Arena. \u201cIt was ideal for us starting out, because we had a lot of full houses and that made it feel big,\u201d said Embry, 80, who is now a senior advisor to the Toronto Raptors. A year later, with the good fortune of a coin flip and the resulting arrival of Lew Alcindor (later Kareem Abdul-Jabbar), the Bucks got big. They jumped from 27 to 56 victories with the dominant rookie and lost in the East finals to the eventual-champion New York Knicks. The next season, once Embry persuaded his old Cincinnati roommate, Oscar Robertson, to accept a trade there , Milwaukee won 66 games and its only NBA championship . The Bucks got into The Finals again in 1974, losing Game 7 at the Arena to the Celtics . Abdul-Jabbar leveraged his way out of Milwaukee to the Lakers after the 1974-75 season, taking his sky-hook success with him (they were 342-150 in six seasons). But an even bigger star arrived two years later. The floor. With Milwaukee\u2019s power brokers eager to promote the city and bolster civic pride, they hit upon an unlikely option: They commissioned pop artist Robert Indiana, a cohort of Andy Warhol most famous for his 1965 \u201cLOVE\u201d design , to create a basketball floor unlike any other. Indiana\u2019s design cost $27,500, was hailed as the \u201conly court that has paint covering the entire surface\u201d and, with its eye-popping use of yellow, orange, red, blue and green, was deemed by Marquette officials as \u201caesthetically distasteful.\u201d Featuring two massive \u201cM\u2019s\u201d embedded in the design, with \u201cMECCA\u201d (for Milwaukee Exposition, Convention Center and Arena) prominently featured at center court, others\u2019 reviews were mixed. Don Nelson, in his first full season as Bucks coach, said: \u201cAt first I thought we had to wear sunglasses because it was so bright.\u201d Doc Rivers, the L.A. Clippers coach who played on that floor while at Marquette and later as a Bucks opponent, said in 2014 for an ESPN documentary on the design: \u201cAs I got away from it, I learned about the history of it and the art of it. That it was an art piece. I was like, \u2018Wow, I never knew that. I thought I was just playing on a confusing floor.\u2019 \u201d * Photo gallery:  Bucks practice on MECCA court Said Marques Johnson, a four-time All-Star with Milwaukee and now a TV analyst with the team: \u201cPeople were all excited, that they were going to have the largest piece of pop artwork in the world. As a player, you\u2019re not overly enamored with that \u2014 you\u2019re like, \u2018I\u2019m just out here to play. As long as you can get some good liftoff and landing spots\u2019 \u2014 but it added to the allure. It brightened up a drab and dusty old arena and put a nice touch on a place that maybe wasn\u2019t that appealing at the time.\u201d The buzz in Milwaukee was exceeded by the floor\u2019s reception nationally, as viewers absorbed it again and again on telecasts. \u201cIt accomplished its goal,\u201d Johnson said. \u201cIt became a talking point, whether it was \u2018the crazy floor,\u2019 \u2018the colorful floor.\u2019 A lot of guys back in those days from opposing teams would say, \u2018What\u2019s it like to play on this psychedelic floor?\u2019 \u201d The original floor still exists and the Bucks initially pitched the NBA on the idea of using it for the game against Boston. Said Godsey: \u201cBut from the standpoint of it being a 60-year-old floor \u2014 that floor predated the Bucks even \u2014 with its dead spots and player-safety issues, they wouldn\u2019t give us the green light for that. So we went to work on [a replica provided by the team\u2019s floor contractor], getting permission from the people who assigned rights for Robert Indiana\u2019s artwork. \u201cIt sort of came down to the wire \u2014 we didn\u2019t know we\u2019d get it done and we had some contingency plans, but this was our hope from the beginning.\u201d Without the replica floor, much of the nostalgia of this #TBT game would be lost on the TNT audience. But its iconic status was elevated in part by the teams that played on it for most of its 11 years of usage at the Arena. From 1979-87, Nelson\u2019s Bucks averaged 54 victories, won their division seven times in eight seasons and made the playoffs each year in a streak of 12 consecutive postseason appearances. Milwaukee\u2019s all-time regular season record in the building was 582-209 (.736), thanks to some key players obtained in the Abdul-Jabbar trade with the Lakers \u2014 Brian Winters, Junior Bridgeman \u2014 and drafting or acquiring others such as Johnson, Sidney Moncrief, Bob Lanier, Terry Cummings, Paul Pressey and Ricky Pierce. \u201cThat\u2019s why I always joke with Lanier, if we could have gotten him maybe two years earlier, it would have made a profound difference,\u201d Johnson said of the Hall of Fame center, who joined the Bucks via a February 1980 trade . \u201cHe still was good, don\u2019t get me wrong, but instead of a 25-point, 12-rebound guy, he was more of a 17-point, eight-rebound player.\u201d As successful as those \u201880s Bucks teams were \u2014 Nelson was named Coach of the Year in \u201883 and \u201885 \u2014 they annually ran into powerhouses from Boston or Philadelphia and never reached The Finals. \u201cAt the time it was frustrating as hell, losing to Boston, losing to Philly, not being able to advance,\u201d Johnson said. \u201cAlways ending up just short. Sweep the Celtics, then run into Moses Malone. But looking back on it, we just lost to better teams. There really wasn\u2019t anything to hold your head down about, when you\u2019re talking Julius [Erving], Moses, Maurice Cheeks and Bobby Jones, or Larry Bird, Robert Parish, Kevin McHale and Dennis Johnson. Those were some good teams.\u201d Johnson laughed as he reflected. He spoke of the small forwards then who served as rivals: Erving, Bird, Bernard King, Walter Davis, Dominique Wilkins. Then he shared this about the only Milwaukee arena in which he played: \u201cThe most personal memory I have is, it was an old school arena so you\u2019ve got the organist, Frank Charles, sitting up in the rafters,\u201d Johnson said. \u201cEvery time I would dunk or catch a lob pass and do some body control or whatever, he would break into \u2018 Daring Young Man on the Flying Trapeze. \u2019 \u201cIf I got a chance, I\u2019d look up at him and give him kind of a wave and he\u2019d give me a nod. That was one of my favorite moments.\u201d Here are some other things you might not know or recall about this storied arena: * The Bucks clobbered Baltimore 151-99 on Jan. 10, 1971, but the final score wasn\u2019t the most memorable moment. That came in the fourth quarter, when Bullets forward Gus Johnson \u2014 long before Darryl Dawkins or Shaquille O\u2019Neal \u2014 shattered one backboard with a monstrous slam dunk. It took 30 minutes to position a replacement hoop. * Not quite a year later, on Jan. 9, 1972 , the defending champion Bucks snapped the Lakers\u2019 still-record NBA winning streak at 33 games as Abdul-Jabbar had 39 points and 20 boards. Milwaukee finished 63-19 to the Lakers\u2019 69-13 that season and lost to Wilt Chamberlain, Jerry West and the rest in the West finals. * Celtics coach Brad Stevens worked in the building once before. He led Butler past UWM in the Horizon League tournament championship game in March 2011. * There was no parking lot for the players, so they parked across State St. on the north side of the arena \u2014 at the McDonald\u2019s franchise owned by Embry. That store got bought out and steamrolled to make room for the Bradley Center. * The location of a garage door on the loading dock allowed Milwaukee\u2019s frigid winter winds to whip through the building and across the court. As a result, Bucks players often practiced in hoodies and sweat pants. Said Johnson: \u201cI was good friends with a lot of the Laker guys, and they would come in in the middle of January. It might be 30-below with the wind chill factor and they\u2019re coming in with their little polyester coats.\u201d * The 1977 All-Star Game was played at the Arena , the league\u2019s first after the NBA\/ABA merger. Five of the 10 starters had come over from the ABA, including the game\u2019s MVP, Erving. That event produced its own iconic pop art courtesy of LeRoy Neiman for its program cover and poster. * The Bucks\u2019 10th season opened with a bang when Abdul-Jabbar, back with the Lakers, punched Milwaukee rookie Kent Benson in the face just minutes into the game . His coaches reportedly had worked Benson into a lather in his first NBA game to play physically against the legendary big man, and Abdul-Jabbar did not take kindly to Benson\u2019s elbow to his midsection. Kareem broke his hand and missed two months, while Benson\u2019s facial fracture was cited as one reason for his career\u2019s mediocre trajectory. * On Dec. 9, 1978, the Chicago Hustle beat the Milwaukee Does 92-87 in what was billed as the first women\u2019s professional game ever. The Does played two seasons in the soon-defunct Women\u2019s Professional Basketball League. Inaugural Bucks coach Larry Costello coached the team in its second season. * Bucks owner Jim Fitzgerald infuriated the Celtics when he lit up a victory cigar \u2014 a dig at the legendary (and still active) Red Auerbach \u2014 after Game 4 of Milwaukee\u2019s sweep in the 1983 Eastern Conference semifinals. Lanier grabbed a courtside microphone to the PA system after the final horn to lead the fans in a \u201cSweep!\u201d chant. * Milwaukee\u2019s first-round triumph over Philadelphia in the 1987 playoffs meant that the great Erving played the final game of his Hall of Fame career at the MECCA. His line: 10-of-24 for 24 points with four rebounds, two assists and three steals in 40 minutes. * In October 1987, in the first McDonald\u2019s Open, the Bucks faced and beat Tracer Milan (featuring star Mike D\u2019Antoni) and the Soviet National Team in an early NBA brush with international competition. Milwaukee forward Terry Cummings was named tournament MVP. Meanwhile, Bucks coach Del Harris said: \u201c[We] left no doubt that if you want to beat somebody from the NBA, you\u2019d better pick on somebody other than the Bucks.\u201d * Payback can bite, as Bird made painfully clear to the Bucks in \u201886 when he led the Celtics to a sweep of Milwaukee in the Eastern Conference finals. It was said that Boston remembered Milwaukee\u2019s sweep antics from \u201883, and Bird was merciless to the end this time. He averaged 25.3 ppg, 9.5 rpg, 8.0 apg and 1.8 spg, scored 17 of his 30 points in the fourth quarter of the May 18 finale \u2014 and from the left corner, sank a 3-pointer as time expired in what became a 13-point victory, walking off the brightly colored even as the basketball swished through . \u201cI hope the other Celtics,\u201d Nelson said, \u201crealize what a privilege it is to play with Larry Bird.\u201d May the folks in Milwaukee realize, so many years later, what a privilege it is to see one more game at their city\u2019s storied and beloved arena. Some other notes to take away from Davis\u2019 monster scoring night: * Davis had 28 points by halftime and 40 through three quarters. * Overall, he was 17 of 34 from the field and 16 of 17 from the foul line. \u201cIt\u2019s tough. It probably wasn\u2019t enough. I missed like three layups at the basket, some chip shots that I normally make,\u201d Davis said after the loss. The new explosiveness was showcased by Jaylen Brown, who celebrated his 21st birthday Tuesday with an opening-quarter slam against the winless Knicks. Brown (23 points on 16 shots) and rookie Jayson Tatum (22 on 15) became the Celtics\u2019 first duo to score at least 20 points in the same game before their 22nd birthday. \u201cThey are young guys,\u201d said Celtics coach Brad Stevens, \u201cbut to us, with the situation we\u2019re in, they\u2019re guys. Like, we need them to be guys. We need them to play well on Thursday.\u201d On Thursday, the Celtics (2-2 after their 110-89 clobbering of New York ) will be on the road for a rematch with the Bucks (3-1), who beat them 108-100 in Boston\u2019s home opener last week. Brown (18.8 points) and Tatum (14.8) rank No. 2 and 3, respectively, in points and minutes, while helping to fill in for All-Star Gordon Hayward, who appears to be out for the season after suffering a gruesome ankle on opening night in Cleveland. \u201cWe\u2019re in a situation right now where we\u2019re going to expect a lot out of those guys and we need them to be great, we need them to be able to respond to adversity, and we need to be able to respond to pats on the back just the same,\u201d Stevens said. \u201cWe have high expectations for them; they should have high expectations for themselves, and they\u2019re getting a great opportunity. So, we need them to continue to be good, and there\u2019s a lot of fun in that, I think.\u201d As much as they miss Hayward and wish he were here, the Celtics remain a team of upside. Apart from Al Horford (31) and Aron Baynes (30), everyone on the roster is 25 or younger. At this early-season moment, the Celtics are defined more by Brown and Tatum than they are by Kyrie Irving, their All-NBA point guard who was acquired from the Cavaliers last summer. \u201cIt\u2019s very obvious,\u201d said Horford of the Celtics\u2019 inexperience. \u201cWe feel it, we see it out there. Even though we have a lot of younger guys, they\u2019re mature beyond their years. It\u2019s not like you\u2019re dealing with the rookie headaches and things like that. But you can really tell it\u2019s game four of the year and we still have a ways to go.\u201d Hayward\u2019s abrupt absence has changed the point of view without altering the ultimate goal. The Celtics still want to contend for championships. In the absence of Hayward, however, they can\u2019t afford to reach for that outcome in the here and now \u2014 not with so much to be learned and proved. Will they be a defense-first team? An up-tempo, share-the-ball team? Those have been traits of Stevens\u2019 preceding four seasons in Boston. But it\u2019s too early to predict the future for this developing roster.  Irving is averaging 20 points and shooting 37.5 percent as he adapts to his new surroundings. He is going to be judged by whether he can take pressure off his young teammates even as he pushes them to thrive ahead of schedule \u2014 a passive-aggressive tack that LeBron James utilized while leading Irving and his fellow Cavaliers to The 2015 NBA Finals in their first season together. The young Celtic most likely to flourish is Brown, the second-year swingman ( and No. 3 pick of the 2016 Draft ) who generated 25 points on opening night while overcoming the shock of Hayward\u2019s gruesome injury. Brown has high hopes for himself across the board \u2014 his long-term goals include serving as president of the NBA Players Association \u2014 but Horford doesn\u2019t want to see him trying to take on too much too soon. \u201cWe just need him to do what he\u2019s been doing,\u201d Horford said. \u201cHe has that capability to be a great defender but also impact the offensive end. We want him to keep developing, to keep growing and improving, and make sure that we\u2019re staying after him and he starts understanding how we want him to play. He\u2019s been doing a good job of that.\u201d Though he has quickly become Boston\u2019s No. 2 scoring option, the Celtics are encouraging Brown to look beyond the numbers. \u201cIt should happen naturally,\u201d said Horford of Brown\u2019s statistical growth. \u201cThere\u2019ll be some nights that he\u2019ll have high-scoring games. There\u2019ll be other nights that he\u2019ll be doing more defensive work. I think it\u2019s impressive because there\u2019s not a lot of guys like him that are able to play defense and offense. He\u2019s usually guarding one of the better guys defensively, and at the same time we\u2019re expecting him to score the ball.\u201d  Tatum, the No. 3 pick last June, has been encouraged by teammates and coaches to hoist up shots. \u201cThat\u2019s the toughest part, me being a rookie and being out there with Al and Kyrie \u2013 instinctively I think, just give them the ball, even though I may be open,\u201d said 19-year-old Tatum, who has also emerged as Boston\u2019s No. 3 rebounder (7.8). \u201cBut it\u2019s good for our team, when somebody\u2019s open, to shoot their shot.\u201d The Celtics opened the second quarter Tuesday with a second-unit lineup meant to force-feed Tatum. Over the next 4:25 he sandwiched a pair of 3-pointers around a fade away, a transition assist, and a block that he turned into a full-sprint alley-oop as Boston stretched its lead out to 20 points. Tatum, who was 1-for-5 from the arc through his first three games, hit 4 of 6 on Tuesday. In the first half alone, he and Brown combined for 30 points \u2013 three fewer than the Knicks. \u201cWe don\u2019t need them to do anything they don\u2019t do well,\u201d Stevens said. \u201cWe just need them to be good at what they do well.\u201d As Brown continues to invest in the details of his development \u2013 extra shooting, weightlifting, individual skills workouts and the like \u2013 he serves as an inspiring role model for Tatum. \u201cIn Jaylen\u2019s case last year, he played really well, and he did what he did really well and he kept going \u2014 (but) there were times when he didn\u2019t,\u201d Stevens said. \u201cAnd I thought the best thing about him was how he just responded regardless. He was great working to get better the next day, regardless of whether the game before had gone well or not. That\u2019s the one thing we can take from that experience that Jayson needs to copy.\u201d They\u2019re not the only Celtics hoping for big steps. Fourth-year guard Marcus Smart has been sidelined the last two games by a sprained ankle, but after losing 20 pounds over the summer there is promise of him fulfilling his potential as a hardcore defender while achieving consistency at the other end \u2014 just in time for him to cash in as a restricted free agent next summer. Forward Marcus Morris, recovering from knee soreness, may make his Boston debut by Halloween, while backup point guard Terry Rozier has already shown that he can fit into a variety of lineups. \u201cWith Gordon\u2019s loss, our help is going to come from our bench and our depth \u2014 from guys like (rookie forward) Semi Ojeyele and once Marcus Morris gets back,\u201d Horford said. \u201cGuys like that are going to be able to step in and help us fill that void, which is hard to do when you have one of your best players out.\u201d Hayward\u2019s injury forced Stevens to simplify the offense. He was investing in cohesion by keeping his starters together on the court until 4:20 remained in their blowout win against the Knicks. \u201cWe just need to do what we\u2019re doing better,\u201d Stevens said. \u201cOur defense is going to have to be really, really good as we grow and learn how to score the ball together.\u201d The defensive principles haven\u2019t changed. \u201cIt\u2019s very similar to last year,\u201d said Horford. \u201cI\u2019m really conscious of talking to the (new) guys and making sure they understand where they need to be, and that they feel comfortable with what we need to do.\u201d When Brown came out with 2:41 left, a group of fans behind the basket shouted happy birthday to him. He waved to them from the sideline. It\u2019s early in his career, but he was already feeling at home. Ian Thomsen has covered the NBA since 2000. MRI results were negative, but Davis remains day-to-day."},{"id":43512,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/horry-scale-eric-gordon-houston-rockets-silences-76ers","date":"2017-10-26","title":"Horry Scale: Eric Gordon's 3-pointer caps off Houston Rockets' rally over Sixers","content":"A reminder on The Horry Scale : It breaks down a game-winning buzzer-beater (GWBB) in the categories of difficulty, game situation (was the team tied or behind at the time?), importance (playoff game or garden-variety night in November?) and celebration. Then we give it an overall grade on a scale of 1-5 Robert Horrys, named for the patron saint of last-second answered prayers. * * * The Philadelphia 76ers will have to chalk this one up as a learning experience. After trailing for most of the game, the Houston Rockets pulled off a late rally \u2013 closing the game on a 9-0 run \u2014 to stun the young Sixers 105-104 on Eric Gordon\u2019s corner 3-pointer. With 6.9 seconds left and the Rockets down by two, Gordon inbounded the ball to Ryan Anderson, who handed off to James Harden going to his left. When the double-team came from Robert Covington and Joel Embiid, Harden stumbled to the floor, dishing the ball to Gordon, who had faded to the corner. With Embiid lunging toward him, Gordon gave the center a pump-fake, took one dribble to his right and launched over the outstretched arm of Covington and silenced the crowd in Philadelphia with the made triple. DIFFICULTY: Gordon took 16 3-pointers (hitting five) on the night, but none was bigger or more difficult than his last. With two long-armed defenders in Embiid (7-0) and Covington (6-foot-9) and little room in the corner, Gordon had to think quickly and launch without hesitation. Gordon is having the best scoring year of his 10-year career, averaging 24.6 points through five games, but is still hitting just 26.8 percent of his 3-point attempts. Gordon didn\u2019t hesitate and there was little doubt this one was going in, though, considering the way the Sixers mishandled the end of the game. GAME SITUATION: Both teams played without key members. The Sixers were without No. 1 pick Markelle Fultz, who is out with a sore right shoulder, and Houston was without starters Chris Paul and Trevor Ariza, placing even more emphasis on the backcourt duo of Gordon and Harden. Gordon (29) and Harden (27) combined for 56 points, but the Rockets found themselves down 104-96 with 3:05 left after a layup from Philly rookie Ben Simmons that had the big Philly crowd of 20,682 fans ecstatic sensing a big win over an elite Western Conference team. But Philly couldn\u2019t convert down the stretch, with J.J. Redick (who finished with a team-high 22 points) missing a pair of 3s and Jerryd Bayless being forced into a terrible shot after Simmons dribbled down the clock on Philly\u2019s final possession. Those miscues led to Houston\u2019s final opportunity, and it only felt fitting that the Rockets would pull this one out. CELEBRATION: As Gordon\u2019s shot dropped in, James Harden, who had fallen to the floor on the play, flopped onto his back and raised both arms in celebration while Gordon raced down court with a single finger raised in the air before being mugged by his teammates at midcourt. The Sixers crowd, which had been energized all game, was left in a stunned silence as the Rockets raced off the floor. GRADE: The winner was nice, but you almost got the feeling that it was coming, even though Gordon was 4-for-15 on 3s before the game-winner, considering the two teams involved and the way Philly faltered down the stretch. Gordon\u2019s shot was nice, and it took some quick thinking and a quick release to get the shot off, but the level of difficulty wasn\u2019t too high. Embiid and Covington did a good job defending the play, taking the ball out of Harden\u2019s hands, but Gordon and the Rockets couldn\u2019t be denied on this night. Three Horrys . But former commissioner David Stern thinks it\u2019s time for a change. Stern sat down with former player Al Harrington, who played 16 years in the league and has since become an advocate and entrepeneur in the medical marijuana business, in a recent documentary on UNINTERRUPTED . Harrington talked to Stern about his tenure as commissioner, his handling of the drug\u2019s use among players and how his perception has changed. \u201cI\u2019m now at the point where personally I think it should be removed from the banned list,\u201d Stern told Harrington. \u201cYou\u2019ve persuaded me.\u201d Stern was commissioner from 1984 to 2014 and helped enforce more strident rules during his tenure. \u201cIt was generally known at some point, until we tightened the rules, that a lot of our players were smoking a lot of marijuana,\u201d Stern said in the interview. \u201cIn fact, some of our players came to us and said, \u2018Some of these guys are high coming into the game.\u2019 But we began tightening it up, and at that time people accepted the generally held wisdom that marijuana was a gateway drug and that if you start smoking, you\u2019re liable to go on to bigger and better stuff.\u201d Stern said in the interview that sports leagues could play a vital role \u2014 working with players\u2019 associations \u2014 in pushing for better understanding of cannabis\u2019 medical benefits. \u201cI think we have to change the Collective Bargaining Agreement and let you do what\u2019s legal in your state,\u201d Stern said. \u201cIf marijuana is now in the process of being legalized, I would think you should be allowed to do what is legal in your state. Now I think it\u2019s up to the sports leagues to anticipate where this is going and maybe lead the way.\u201d In a statement, NBA spokesman Mike Bass says the league\u2019s position remains unchanged. \u201cWhile Commissioner Silver has said that we are interested in better understanding the safety and efficacy of medical marijuana, our position remains unchanged regarding the use by current NBA players of marijuana for recreational purposes.\u201d"}]
